Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauterizations of pleurisy with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia as big as your thumb; and dry it, and make it so thick and so long as the thickness of your thumb; and moisten it in oil, and hold it at the fire, and cauterize .i. cautery between the ribcage and the neck, and two small cauterizations one a little below in the part that is under the beard; and two cauterizations between the lowest ribs and the last, declinating backwards a little; and one cautery in the breast, and one above the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two at the sides of the chest after the cautery which is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make it open as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said some old man that someone uses the fire cautery similar to the razor, and warms it up and puts it between the ribs, so long as it comes to that abscess; and suddenly the pain bursts out, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear for the patient's death now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! "De la mie" est une expression française qui signifie "du pain" ou "le centre". Est-ce que vous avez une citation ou un texte lié à cela ?
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	Merci pour le contexte ! Il semble que nous ayons affaire à un texte médical ancien.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	There is one manner such that you make three cauterizations, or four, along the length of the vein, according to the figure of the liver cauterization that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cauterization, and let the patient be seated on his back; and another cauterization manner is such that you warm up the cauterization which has two ners, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the key which is at the vein, or the patient's ribs come towards the left, and are the elevations from which you lift the key according to the key, according to the length of the body, and the cauterization be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After you put the two needles inflamed as long as the key is pierced from the other side, and then pull out the cauterization, and thus there will be four; and if you see it, so cauterize with all the cauterization at three needles.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when he has gotten a burn for a long time, and this is worse than the other cures mentioned before.

de la hainche	of the hip

Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make more of them; and if he knows that the pain lies under the knee towards the thigh, then you make a cautery at the knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not cauterize too much so that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause more harm and contraction to the patient.

Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which a certain man was cured of the pain in the groin and sciatic vein, and he highly praised it, and says that one did not do another cure, and that he was healed at once when this cure was done, and he had bathed himself as it teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in the same manner that you take green and fresh and dry verdigris and grind it very much with a pint of fat, and put it on the groin and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain holds, and bind it; and let him leave it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then have him enter into a bath until his body is somewhat warmed up, and have him enter into bed, and the pain will go away altogether and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cauterization for such medications, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with thorny fire, it helps a lot; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and put it on the hollow between the big toe and the other that is called foscele.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Then take thorny fire that is dry, and set it on the fire until it becomes charcoal, and put it on the linen, and let it stay until it cools down; and do this again in this manner, and do not stop doing so until you think by reasoning that it will reach to the navel, and the pain will cease; and this method of cauterization is called "cautery of thorny fire".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or percussion or too great evacuation, or from seeming of cold matter spread out, no one of these appearances is worth cauterizing, except that which comes from infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after that the sick person be freed of pills made from fetid things or other semblances, and one makes it on their back, there where the pain holds, three lines marked with ink, and in each line 5 cauters or more according to virtue and quantity that the sick person can bear; and the cauter is made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see, make 3 cauters or 4 at the middle-cautery "clavile" according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have tight limbs when they awaken, and pain; and you find in the last vertebra of the back and on the appearance that comes above the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it heal, then cauterize at the cautery of the back according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If you apply a red hot cautery to each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with a burning cautery that is 2 or 3 lines long, and the points are close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure has healed as much as it is clean according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring a cautery near the elbow where there is a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by a swelling that spreads to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in feet, which they call "podagre" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, so it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and be the cauteries olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you touch above the face of the foot, then make a cautery all over with the hot cautery that we call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knee and to other joints, and this occurs many times, then make a cautery above each kneecap 3 or 4 times on each part, to a full olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do it again, but don't hold your hand out there until the wood of the cure is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and on the back, administer the cauterization that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the tumor two lines; and if there remains no pain in the wrists, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come just to the armpits or just to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good treatment for the patient and apply medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and purge his phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	...the treatment for hernia.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an obstruction comes in the intestines, and the bowels descend to the groin and it is new, so it is necessary that when you see it needs to be cured, do not cut into him that day; and let him use things which loosen the belly, so that the feces descend from his belly; then make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are relaxed, and remove them to your right, and sign with a mark under the obstruction above the bone of the elbow, and in all a sign which is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with which it is the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as he remains white and spits up pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the intestines to their place; and the attendants bind his hand so that they do not return behind; and make good work on the thighs for the patient, and put beneath him a cushion and a servant on the thighs, and another on the back which binds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign on all your hand, and hold it straight and hold until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you feel the bone; and be careful subtly that the intestines do not burst when you make the cautery, lest you burn him; and lest through this the patient die, or some other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you don't come close to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to their size, and also for grown people as large as their measure; afterwards cure the place of the cauterized spot with butter so that the scab be removed; afterwards cure other ointments until they are healed, and have the patient lie on his back 40 days in order that the wound be well closed; and it is necessary that the swellings be allowed to last for a long time, so that the boils not burst when he will go into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And afterwards, when he will want to get up, have him given a well-made bandage and wear it for 40 more days; and take good rest, that he not work much and be careful of excessive drinking and eating, and high fevers; and when he does this teaching then is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say next the cure of cutting as is written in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When fistulas come into other bodies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, then make the cautery of the cautery in its quantity, and let it burn the third part of the skin; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients said that one must cauterize with the cautery at three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first mark indicate the middle of the fistula and make one line above it over the fistula, and another below, and hold your hand in it all along the entire cautery groove.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and less effective.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes into any member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine does not work, then it is necessary that he be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cautery be according to the length of the member, and its tenderness and weakness, and its virtue and its location, and its twistings and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cauterization, that's well; if this one doesn't work, repeat the other cauterization on him, for it's a custom that it should move to the member that is closest, therefore you must do the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of wound healing (or surgery)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The members are helped sometimes by cauterization with great effort, and the same disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see it being cauterized, take note if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is healed according to what we have said in the division, and it does not spread nor remain, and you doubt that corruption will corrupt the entire patient, then do V cauterizations on his head: I in the middle of the head very deep, and the other towards the forehead to the end of the eyebrows; and II above the two horns, and I behind on the nape; and hold your hand so that the cauterization comes as far as the bone, and until the rinds come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can issue forth; and cauterize on the nose according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is spread throughout; and it is manifestly being wasted, it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries on the head which we have said, and one cautery on the nape, and two cauteres on the spine of the neck, and five cauteres on the spine of the back, and one large one on the scrotum and another nearby, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the thighs, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and in the pits of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are behind the spine, so you do not burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the fist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	Know that the more I do of cauterizing, the greater the help and benefit it brings; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cauterization as much as the healthy body feels pain, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	It is necessary that the cauterizing be large and small according to the members and joints, as you will find it in the manner of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure, heal the place with flour a few times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation comes to any member and is cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then make a cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be one part entering into the depth of the wound; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at any time one does cautery on the hand and foot and back, from the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is removed the swelling; and however no one should intervene if they are not knowledgeable about the members and exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	Of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has grown old, and medical remedies are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery that is deep, according to the size of the skin, until the ulcer is removed, and its color is changed; then cure it with flour of wheat and lentils mixed with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of goose and blood of crane, each one in equal part; and mix all together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it at high place until it's healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil comes at the beginning and you stop up the view, if one cauterizes with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the boil.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise ones said that one should also do cautery in the middle of the boil; and yet this does not seem to me good, because I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it come about once or twice; and a more direct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circule", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of a swelling which cannot perish (die)
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays death or because of the superfluity that it causes or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old) and he has pus in his blood, or because of the weather; and you see it hastening to kill: then cauterize him around with many small cauteries which prick; afterwards leave him so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery until its form is like this: (note: there seems to be a blank line or omission in the original text at this point)
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand into the midst of that disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced the core, and be such cauters that the patient feels them all over in such a way that the course of the pus is elevated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards cure him until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure by fire with iron (presumably referring to a surgical procedure using cautery)
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a rotting of the member, for it rots the members as much as fire does dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the place that can suffer a cautery together with fire, then heat up the cauters small and big hammer-like little and big, according to what is needed for the place where the sickness is; after you have cauterized from all sides until you have extracted all the corruption and nothing remains of it, so that everything which is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for 3 days, and apply oil to the places that have been cauterized so that they may boil, until all the burns from fire are gone, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the ointment cure, a scab forms.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after 3 days that a healthy scab does not form, it is good; and if not, then recommence the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this mixture is sometimes cured with medicinal poultice instead of fire cauterization; but nonetheless fire cauterization is a greater aid, and I have already said the cure of the medicinal poultice in the division: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the splinters that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often times it happens that on the feet outside a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large foul growth that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is in two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say fire cauterization, and hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cauterization is that you heat the cautery so that it also shines like a well-whittled penknife, and let it be made of good iron to the measure that it can pierce the tumor from all sides, and have subtle edges; then place it very hot on the tumor, and turn your hand completely around the tumor until it comes to the temperature of the body; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to suppurate; then make a poultice of bitter wild rue pounded with oil, and let the poultice remain over all night, and the growth will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place with ointment by applying grease so long as it is sound.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted to the outside of the body, and often occur in hands and feet, it is necessary that you bring them water hot cauterization; and so: take a pipe of bronze or iron, or an awl of copper, and put on the nail and the root of it, namely porridge warts; and place the pipe so that it touches all around, then put in some hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the pipe comes to the root of the nail, and can find hot water deep enough just to the root; and let the sick person suffer a little the mordication of the hot water an hour; then leave it thus, and it will deracinate itself entirely with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do the same with another, until you have extracted all those that are in the body, then treat them of unguents which cause corruption.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold or fever quartan or another thing, then it is necessary that you make 4 cauterizations or 5 on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one on the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped part; he will stop trembling, and hasten to health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	The cure for boils or pustules (puans in Old French). Here is a continuation of the text:
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Some times appear on the outside of the body blisters, or suppurating boils, which come from thick corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	it is necessary at first when they appear to make a cautery over the head of each boil: a subtle cautery of hazel wood whose point has been grasped in the fire, or of a long aristolochia root, or a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes after cauterizing them at the beginning when they appear in this manner, they cannot grow outwards, but the superfluous matter from which they come is ruptured and they are healed; but it should be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there occur great hemorrhages of blood from the artery that is cut to the wound that comes first, or to the incision of the apostema, or to the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nonetheless when this happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your index finger over the wound of the vein, and press very hard until the bleeding ceases under your finger, and no more blood flows; then take several small and large olive oil cauteries as many as are needed, heat them up so that they are all red; then grasp one, either a large or small one according to the wound and its location where the artery runs, and put the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts forth when you lift your finger off the vein, and the cautery is spent, then take another one quickly from among those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this until the bleeding is stopped. Be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient. And know that when blood flows from an artery, it can hardly be stopped on its own when the artery is large, unless it is done in one of the four ways we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it is not already tied off, or by tightly tying a thread, or by applying medications that have the power to stop bleeding; and it should be closed and tightened properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will remind them of the danger of tightly tying a ligature or putting hot things on it, or similar things, if they do not know what they are doing.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he does not have a surgeon or physician present, then he should put his index finger over the wound of the vein just as we said, and press hard until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and he should not move his finger, but rather wet it with cold water often until it is very cold so that the bleeding is frozen and thickened and stopped; and he should make inquiries ahead of time for things that will be needed from cauteries and medications.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on surgical remedies.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or with hot medicine, and the instruments and causes and reasons and forms of cauterizations; and I placed that chapter at the beginning just up to a point, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that you find what you want more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and because of that it is necessary to be more careful.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there are many times an evacuation of blood when opening the vein, and making an incision above a pustule, and caring for wounds, and extracting splinters, and making an incision on the bone, and similar things; or else there is doubt and fear, and the patient comes to more harm.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	for they come from those who are so beset by their disease that they die easily due to the ignorance of their condition and the greatness of their wickedness; and with these one must be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And from those who give you their opinion, and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but place greater caution in your honor than in your greed, and do not give foolishly but wisely to those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can have taken and gained; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients for whose salvation it shall be converted; and these things will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe with the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen. (This is a final blessing, typical in medieval texts.)
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter in sections, as I was explaining by chapters, according to what is written before the chapter on cauterizations, which I explained from beginning to end for you, so that you would find it easier to understand the things of which you will need. (This is a conclusion and final statement, wrapping up the explanation of the chapter.)
dou chief plein d’aigue	A vessel full of water. (This appears to be a simple phrase or description, possibly referring back to some earlier context in the text where the use of a vessel was mentioned.)
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the cord compresses too strongly the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a reason that is unknown. (This phrase appears to be a medical explanation or warning about a possible cause of a specific illness.)
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in children, and with all that I've seen the death rate has been high; and because of this it seems to me that it's not worth the effort to treat them. (This phrase appears to be a conclusion drawn by the author based on their experience and observations.)
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose eyes were full of water, and the head was swelling every day so much that it could no longer be sustained; and he was so weak that he seemed to be dead, and this weakness is assembled under the bone above the eye socket, between the skull and the bone; and the operation is like this: if the weakness is between the skull and the bone, and the tumors are small, you make an incision in the head of a width of two fingers, as long as the weakness runs; and here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the swelling is under the bone, and you see signs that the corners of the head are open on each side, and when you press it with your hand from the inside, it springs up high, and it does not return to its original shape: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision extract all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After hold the tears of herbs and powder, and put wine and oil in it, and let it be like that until the fifth day; then loosen it, and cure the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head sweat equally, and give food to the patient dry meat of soup until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to make the incision is that you look where the swelling of the abscess and the drainage are assembled; because sometimes it is in front, sometimes at the back, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut there where the abscess opens and the drainage is collected, and make the incision as far as you can, but be careful not to cut the artery; and if you see a lot of bleeding, let it flow, so that the patient may die from blood loss and the evacuation of the swelling.
de reume	It seems like we've reached the end of this medieval medical text! "De reume" is likely a phrase to conclude the passage, possibly meaning "of swellings" or "on the topic of swellings". If you have any more texts to transcribe or questions about these passages, feel free to ask!
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease that is called "catarre" (likely referring to an abscess or tumor in the groin or armpit) and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last cure is to cauterize with what will close the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary then that the patient covers their eyes; after they rub the place with a rough cloth so that the arteries appear, then extract the patient's neck to the whole cloth; then see where the vein bleeds, and the places of one and the other are behind the ears, and they are puffed up; then mark the places with tar, then cut one and the other from an awl sharp as two parts, so that the blade comes until the bone, and this is on the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see fit, insert the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting also as two blades through the middle.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood sprays upward continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the vein does not open to the touch, then you must measure the length of the space of three fingers, and then sign over it and sew just to the bone; and what is needed for blood to be let out is six pints, and perhaps a little more or less, according to how the patient can endure, and the repletion of the vein; then look at the wound: if there remains on the bone a point of pus, then clean it so that abscesses do not come in, then bind up the wound and apply ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient headache comes, and sharp catarrh, by reason of the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and old severe fever and similar things, and all manner of medical treatments help him not, then we cut out the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the sick person makes themselves go bald on their temples, and listen to the artery which opens in the temple, for it beats well and pushes out quite a lot in some men who are too cold; and if it is visible, then the sick person ties their own hair with some cloths, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and heats up the area with hot water until the artery shows manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape off the skin lightly until you come to the vein, then pull it upwards with forceps, and part well from the threads that are under each part; and if the vein is delicate, turn it at the point of a needle, then tie on that part according to the length of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cauterized, then the blood will not all ooze out.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And remove the blood from two to three cells, and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two knots with a strong double thread of silk, so that no infection comes before the wound closes and bleeding stops; then cut off the excess that is between the two knots at the same hour, and afterwards, if you see fit, cauterize it with a cauterizing knife until the bone, as long as the fingers are cut off. This is the main work, if the sick person has no fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is helpful to finish the wounds: for that reason it is of greater help to the wounds.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	When it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made bandages; and when you untie them, be careful to use dry medicines that make flesh grow, and bandages, until they are healed; and if there is bleeding from the artery as much as you work, hasten to cauterize by fire, or fill the place with vitriol and hold it in your hand so that the bleeding is stopped; and if you do not have this present, put on the place your thumb so long as the bleeding is congealed, and bind the place with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be careful as it is necessary; and what is more fragile and lighter in the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein with a trenching cautery cutting to two parts, but the trenching should be well spread so as to keep the heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instruments are too thin, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two blades one inch of space, and then when you mark to enclose the two places, and you lay the hot iron on them so that it comes up just to the bone, and cut the vein in two pieces; and be separated between the two cuts because they are not completely joined by this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	It seems you've started a new sentence.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from the veins that are on the root of the eye's forehead, and it does not benefit from the care of medicine made there, and you see the face of the patient redden, and feel the front ambulation as if with tremors; and since they are swollen and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids are fallen, and are scalded the eyelids, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it "cure contuse" in the past, and this is what you do for the patient who has this disease: let him have hairs on his forehead, then make three cuts on the forehead evenly spaced according to its length; and one of the cuts should be as two thumbs deep from the middle to the back, and the other two should be as two thumbs on either side of the papers [i.e. the skin], and keep away from the incision of the arteries which are on either side of the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the lower jawbones, and make each wound three fingers wide across the joints; and have a piece of sponge and a lot of cloth ready to absorb the blood, then insert the spatula as in this shape.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	deals with the incisions made on the forehead, specifically the part that is between the two incisions, up to the second incision, near the temple. The instructions are to:

des poilz des papieres	It seems like we've taken a turn from the medicinal instructions!
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai. Then sign on top of the paper a figure like a myrtle leaf, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see the paper rising which is divided in two.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if to someone who needs it you need to sew great quantity of paper according to what the paper is moistened; then take all the seam on the two lines that you have signed, and start from the large tear up to small; and one of the tears be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the thread into one of the two angles that are sharp, then scrape it entirely; then sew together the two lips with a stitch of an awl on all fine woolen thread, and wipe away the blood, and make dry the superfluity of threads above the two warts on all sticky things, if you see to do this; and if not, then have no care, then leave the seam and the threads up to three days or four; then treat the wound without seam with drying and constricting things, for the paper revives with the union of the flesh and the assembly of it, but the seam is dead (as said the ancients), and this work without fear; and there is another manner: and it is that you sign the paper on a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have told, at three threads severed according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take care of those who rise to moderate strength equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you have no power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, so take a needle where it has two threads, and put one thread through the figure; and put the other thread next to the large lip, and the second thread next to the small one, and assemble between your fingers the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above which you have marked, as we have said, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is sound; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments; and sometimes happens that the hairs on the paper are converted: so it behooves you to use what we have said about incising; but the stitches in both are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of cracks is in this form: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole inside according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is; and take care of the two ends of each part where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other delicately above what rises from the paper of oil, and strain the two cracks from the two parts together; and leave it so for some days, and the skin that has been strained will die and turn dark and peel off, until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it tarries, if the abscess has great force, then cure it until it is sound; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper is lifted, and the hairs can no longer protrude; and this is the shape of the two stitches that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The stitches are made as follows: you take a very fine needle, and put one thread of silk in it, then assemble the threads and tie them together delicately, and make sure that the length of the threads is about the width of your palm; then order another thin thread of silk to pass through the whole thread, and tie the end of the thread; then put the patient's head in a healthy place, and expose it to sunlight so that the stitches become visible, because this is a very delicate and fine stitch. Then take the needle and go all around the root of the hair next to the wound, and make a hole in the paper as quickly as you can until you reach the natural hair; then pull out the hair from below the stitches up to the natural hair, and put that hair into the stitches, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand gently until all the hairs come out of the stitches along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the thread is pulled and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull the thread from underneath all of the thread that you have ordered, until the thread comes out through the pores above and you see it with your own eyes. Then you will pull out the thread and the stitches, and close your eye and let it rest for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the scar heals; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural eyebrows, and lift them up together as they grow longer, and then lift them up.
de la porriture de l’oil	Il semble que nous avons terminé les instructions sur le traitement des poils et que nous sommes maintenant passés à un autre sujet : "la porriture de l'oil".
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness which is called "aleacrati" or the purring comes into the eye, so there are two ways in it: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And occurs by sudden onset of a wound, or an incision, or a cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of treating it is that you cut open the sudden union, and separate the lips of it, and put in linseed tents, and tie so that it be healed; and it is not necessary that you use in its cure things that dry up and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than the first; but I work with soothing things, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or almond paste and linseed oil cooked together, and anointed with it in a cloth, and I treat them like that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you watch out for it so that it does not suddenly close up again in its former form; and these treatments that we have said are nothing other than remedies against this illness returning in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	The fatty substance that comes into the eye.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is located below, is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.

The accident comes from a wound and tearing and cautery and similar things; and the way of working in it is that you take a needle, with which it has a double thread, and drive it into the flesh, and make it pierce from left to right so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh; then tie the flesh above all the needle, and bind it with a broad strap.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the tear, and turn the paper over, and make two tears on either side inside the paper; and be the eyes of the two tears at the two angles of the incision that you have sewn up, and be made one angle so that when they are joined together, the shape will be as the shape of a letter which is called "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity of its edges which is beneath the paper; then join the two severed parts and sew them with a thread of linen; then do the care of what we have said about soothing medicines and bandages until it is healed.

dou soudement de la papiere	the sudden tearing of the papyrus
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez. de l’ungle de l’oil	De l'ungue de l'oeil (in English: "of the eyelid of the eye")

Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee. de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	It seems like we're still looking at an old medical text from the past.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance. des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes

de la fistule de l’oil	It seems I was translating a medical text on eye care, specifically related to the removal of external veins from the eye (perhaps a type of eye surgery). The phrase "de la fistule de l'oil" can be translated to English as "of the fistula of the eye". A fistula is an abnormal connection or passageway between two body parts, and in this context, it might refer to a abnormal connection or hole in the eye.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	A "fistule de l'oil" that is not healed by cautery and hot medicine, as I mentioned before, is called an "arissati" fistula. When you cure it with a scalpel and remove all the moist tissue that remains there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and blackness, then replace it with all of the instrument by which this shape was created; and it is called "sharp head", and it should be made of iron into one head red, and should be pointed like a file so as it is in this present shape:
