Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it back on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a bit as much as you know that this corruption is removed; and do this repeatedly, then restore the place with medicinal ointments.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the swelling is closed up and flesh has formed, and the body of the abscess is closed up and remains in this way for 40 days, and it does not reopen and is not inflamed, and no bad occurrence comes from it, you should know that it is healed. If not, then there is no other cause except to bring the fistula back into the navel according to this shape: and it is that you uncover with iron a second time, by sharp medicines, and when it has been uncovered take the forceps according to this shape, and make the handle of the forceps be attenuated all the way to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place him on the bone next to the wound, and move your hand away from his eye I put there, then turn it all the way back to the force until it pierces the bone and the patient will feel it if he holds his hand over his navel; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh comes out and hardens the place, let the matter go into the navel; it is a more gentle thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open wide and do not bother at all, nor decrease, you should bind the patient; then heal him; then put on him a compress made of aloes, aloe, incense, and sarcocolle; then strain the eye and fill it with bands and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and double each one in four, and then place one above the other according to the quantity that the eyes need; then bind tightly over with a durable band, and reapply the compresses to suck without hurting; then remove the compresses and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the compress becomes moist, you should tighten it; then remove the compress after a day and a night, and if you see the eye restored, it is good; if not, then repeat the dressing and the cloths and the compress and the compresses until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	tear of the vitreous humor
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the vitreous humor breaks into threads, then swells and comes out of the eye in fibers like a grain of resin, and it is painful to see; then if you see it swollen, the procedure is such that you insert an awl into the root of the lower part, up to the upper part, then insert another awl where there is a double thread from the eyelid; and make it penetrate, and leave the first awl in its place; then cut the loose end of the double thread and bind a part of the vitreous humor around it, and tighten it well; then remove the awl and apply a soft cloth soaked in egg white to the eye; and let it stay until the threads stick with the vitreous humor; then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is bound by the vitreous humor on each side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye looks large and swollen, then pierce it with a fine needle that comes from deep within the eye, and clean out the excess moisture of the albugine (a transparent layer in the front part of the eye) and lower the eye, and enter into it as soon as possible; then draw it out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bottom of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not far from the bowel that is gathered in the eye, resembling an arrow descending, and it is not water; and the way of its appearance in the operation is such that you have the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take his head between your hands by both parts, and pull so that you see the bowel come up to your eyes; then let it be fixed, and do not descend and remove the light, and see the patient's things as he usually sees them; and if it does not descend under, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bowel is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Sit the patient between your hands, then take the sharp spatula and place it on the conjunctiva of the eye that has issued pus; follow the course of the conjunctive with the conjunctiva and cornea, so that the bowels issue; and when they are issued, distill hot vinegar mixed with honey into the eye; or boil water and fenugreek in honey, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	This text appears to be a medical description from medieval France, specifically dealing with eye problems. The phrase "des aigues de l'oil" translates to "waters of the eye".
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the similar waters in division, and what is necessary to pierce; act according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your crossed hands, far from light for the sun, and bind the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is on the left, or in your right hand if it is on the right; then take with your right hand, if the eye is on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or with your left hand if it is on the right; then place the point of the instrument next to the cornea by the width of a grain in the white part of the eye near the smaller eyelid; then insert the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces through the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes out empty; and it is necessary that the depth of the path of almagda be exactly to the bottom of the measurement of the length from the tip of the pupil to the end of the black part; and this is the cornea of the eye; if you see bone in that paper because of the clarity of the conjunctiva, and then place the instrument up to where the water is, then press under a path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water falls now, the patient sees before him and the instrument is in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the water rises again in the second vein, put the force with the instrument, and when it is well fixed and does not rise, then extract it very gently by turning your hand slowly and slowly; and then put back into the water a string or thread, and lift out the eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put behind the stitched or moistened linen in rose oil and white of egg, and tie with healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those who are of our time, put on a common broth with abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the alum cannot enter the eye by its hardness, for there are some men whose eyes are very hard, then you should take the instrument that is called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then perforate the conjunctiva alone, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put in alum very gently, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a suitable bed, where he sleeps on his back in a dark room; and be careful of all movements, and give him light foods, and let him not move his head nor to the right nor to the left, and leave him tied according to his condition until three days; then release him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then remove the bandage up to seven days; and it is not necessary that you do this now in the surgery or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you wait, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses form, instruct the patient to loosen the eye in front of the seventh day, and apply a poultice that soothes abscesses; and when it is calmed, loosen the bandage and place on its face an orrilliet for covering any day, and let it be so in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then the patient goes to and fro, and turns into his cases; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Irak (or Iraq), who said that in his peaceful land, they made a small alum perforation (alberit), through which the fever was sucked out, but I have never seen anyone do it in our territory, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the shapes of alum crystals, because whoever doesn't know them sees them, and they are pure sulfur.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their top is the same subtlety (as alum), and their bottom is in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the navel
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or engendered diverse boils attached, of which some resemble scorpions at the sight of feet; and if they have such that their boil is inflamed with bad color, and if they have a foul-smelling boil of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore of those boils which are foul-smelling and not inflamed, it is necessary that you have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the onion juice on those boils, and treat them hot; then grasp what you can with a sharp spatula from one part, as long as you know that boil is entirely loose.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be scraped off, you should open it all up with the sharp and light tools, until nothing is left; and if it's a swelling or a boil, if the scab comes off as it should, and if they are malignant boils, then hasten to cauterize them until the scab is dried out and the moles are completely removed. Then pour on oil, vinegar, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the pus works, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that he is clean; and if the moisture does not perforate as it should, know that there is raw flesh in the bone above, to which instruments cannot come to cut: then you must put a thread of linen about a palm thick, and as black as your hands, with between each knot an interval of about an inch or less; and have the patient put the end of the thread into his nose at its greatest power, and draw it out smelling until it comes down through the nose into the mouth; and many times do thus the children in school, and this is a light thing for one who wants to do it; then take hold of the head which comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head which comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other as they are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know that the wound has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the son, let out the blood, and soak the son in Egyptian oil, and put it back in its place just like before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that is remaining of flesh; and then put on a bandage of linen some days until you are healed, and if it has need of dry medicines, use them; and this is the shape of the instrument to purify the head, by which we distill oils and medicines into it:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or alum, resembling an open lamp like a flask, and it conducts in the same way; and if you see one, make a closed flask, and it should have instruments for purging the chief; and it should have a handle at the top to hold it when heating oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the navel
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times, a disease called "telul" arises on the navel, and grows and becomes large over time, so that it is visible to look at. And in order to cure it, you should remove it at the beginning, and take out all its roots; then apply hot cautery or burning medicine to it. If one waits too long to remove it until it has grown large, beware of the fact that it may be hard, have a fine color, and poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an infected boil, for when you cut into it even once, great harm comes to the patient. And if the boil is of soft touch, not of fine color, and one sees that it can be completely removed, then empty the patient's body and the boil's roots patiently, and treat the area with dry and binding things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the navel is cut open and cleaned out
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these worked-out cartilages, it profits little, or rather, for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then that it does to whoever it happens to, if you observe whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then you sew up the two lips with a seam, and you take care of it until it heals; and if the lips are already healed from one part and from the other, it is necessary for you to scrape off all parts of their crust until they heal, then assemble the two lips with a seam, and bind them, and sprinkle upon sprinkles of dragon's blood powder, and powdered incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of poultice of quick lime or another binding poultice, and let it stay until it dries out by itself, then take care of it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching the wound is that you assemble the edges: either with needles, as we have said in the belly wound stitching; or with a thread, as I have already told you.
des apostemes des levres	of boils on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have within their lips a hard boil, resembling grains of millet, and smaller and larger ones. Then it is necessary to turn the lips inside out, and cut on each node, and take them with pincers and cut in each part; then apply a poultice to the area after the incision, made from vitriol powder, until the scab is dried up; and then apply oil, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, a piece of gum tissue attached to the gums appears, which the ancients called "albulus". It is necessary that you hold it with forceps and cut at its root, and let the bleeding or scab dry out; then put on the area vitriol powder or other binding and drying powders. And if that piece of gum tissue comes back after the incision, and many times appears, you should cut it a second time and cauterize it: if it does not come back again after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments to cut.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and bitter; and sometimes they are black and greenish-yellow and worm-like, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is foul-smelling. It is necessary that you make the patient sit in your hands, and their jaws be in your holy place, and remove the teeth or scabs where they appear, until nothing remains; and similarly do with blackness and greenness and yellowness and other stains, until they are removed; and if at first cause one removes them, it is good; but if not, repeat the second day and the third, until you have removed everything. And know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work shows, because the raspers used to remove the teeth from outside have different shapes than those used to remove between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay as long as you can from extracting it, because this should not be done; for it is a very high procedure, and one must have no excuse for doing so.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to have blood drawn, it is necessary that you are certain of the vein being punctured.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain would leave the patient, and they believed it was the good vein, and had blood drawn from that one; and yet the pain does not depart by this means until the bad vein is extracted, for we have already seen this happen to these patients; and when you are certain of the good vein, then it is necessary that you scrape around the vein on all sides with a sharp spoon, hard enough to keep the gum from getting in the way; then move it with your thumbs or fine pincers at the first touch and touch again, until they are well closed, then tighten the pincers; and have the patient's vein between your knees, and hold it still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the vein properly without breaking it, and if it does not start to bleed, then take one of these instruments and insert it into each part lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and munched, you must fill it with cloths, where the perforation are; and if you strain gently with tweezers, so that it does not break when straining; and it is necessary to work carefully around the gum for to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you must beware so that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and tell the patient to return with greater pain from the evil of the root than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act in the same way as ignorant physicians, who by their haste and boldness break sometimes the carriage, and do not bring what we have said; but bring sometimes through the decay of the roots a great illness from the roots which remain, or because they break the carriage, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is loose, wash the place with vinegar or ash and oil; and if there comes bleeding from it, which happens often, fill the place with vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tweezers, through which you must remove the teeth first, are with long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick limbs so that they do not bend when you pull them, and be made of good iron well-made, and have teeth to firmly hold.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains on the outside, then you must put moistened cotton or a poultice on it for one day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the place is softened, then put in the pliers which are called "algefri", because the bone seems to be like a beak of a bird; and they should be made inside as if with a file and that is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, you should uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and I put the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a plane, through which this is their shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps through this, it is good; if not, you help with all the pliers, through which these shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help yourself with that instrument which has two jaws, through which this is their shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other fixings that are in front of the reason for the teeth, and this instrument which looks like large pliers, through which this is their shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is strong so that it cannot break, and you know that there are many instruments for the teeth; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and wise and subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are such diseases where the old did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of cases, and they do not break the jaw or the other bones, if they can help it, then they search for the instruments that I have told you about, and they ask for gestures, through which this is their shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be strong and hold well so that the bone does not slip away, but rather can hold and remove it; and then restore the place to medicines suitable for this, and if there is pus in the bone and it is small, you should use all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural shape and the form is ugly, and especially in young women, you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and cannot be polished or filed: then pull it. And if it is stuck with the tooth, take this instrument through which this is its shape, and it looks like a small beak, and is made of iron with a sharp point at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and in your hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that you can file it, take this file through which this is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file through which we make needles; and gently file the tooth in short strokes, so that it does not move until it is smooth. Then take the plane at the end of all this scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, you need to file the sharpness so that it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the word:
quant li dent lochent	Quand il sont déchiquetés. (When they are chipped)
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loose from falling or striking a blow, and the patient cannot press on it without it falling out, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, and they are of no use; then they must be restrained with a gold thread, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold ones never change; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the width of the space between the teeth; and if you see the tooth moving, take the thread and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth between the new ones, if there are one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering up as far as the part where you began, and restrain your hand subtly and skillfully, as long as it does not move; and let your thread be tied at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then twist the hooks of the thread with a pair of pincers and assemble them, and point between the healthy tooth and then put it in such a way that it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose, or the strings break, so tie it again with another string. If it stays like this for its entire time, it will serve thus, and it is the form of the teeth and the shape of the joining of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is loose, then put it back in its place, fresh and fresh, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and patient meddle with it. And at times a shape like that of a cow's bone tooth is made, and it is placed in the spot where the defect is, and it is tightened just as we have said, and it stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the ligament from the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this lien comes from under the tongue or natured, that is, when one is born like this; or by accident of a wound that has healed; and the work is such that you operate on the patient's mouth and have his head in your healthy one, and lift up the tongue; then twist the nervous lien from the large part, as long as the tongue is freed from its place, and if there is stiffness or knot, and it is a sudden wound, then insert the unguent and twist with the large one that ligament; and take care that the cut is not too deep, for the artery that is under; and when you have done this, then lift up the head of rose water and azil, or cold water, and put a linen tent over the tongue; and each night, bind the patient so that the swelling cannot set.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding comes from the scab, then place vitriol plaster on the wound; and if the blood flows, then apply slow fire cauterization, which is good for this; then treat with another treatment until they are healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the swelling is of a color that is white or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is an ulcer; and if it is declining towards pus, and there is moisture, inject oil, and make a fine poultice around it, and deliver him from one part to another; and if blood flows into your work, put on vinegar compress as long as it is stopped up, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the bad matter; then raise the place of silk and linen, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes swellings come inside the throat called "godath", and they are properly called the II almonds; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it's a hard abscess of small sense and fusse color, then don't touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, then don't touch it with iron, also because of the bleeding; but let it stay until it is dead, and then you will cut it out, or else it would break apart by itself; and if it is of white color and greenish, and the root is thin, then have the instrument ready to cut, but first look and see if the abscess has cooled down and is eased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and his face should be turned towards it, and he should open his mouth and the servant should take hold of him by the shoulders, and press the tongue firmly against the instrument itself, whether it is made of silver or subtle bronze like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the swelling, then take a thorn and insert it into the almond, and draw out the bad matter from above as much as you can; and remove any thread or string that may be attached, then scrape off with the instrument, which is its shape, resembling a forceps. And although its head is curved, one end to the other, and are very sharp, and it's made of iron or lead:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument available, then scrape off with pincers, which is its shape.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be pointed on one side and flat on the other. And when you have scraped one of the almonds, scrape the other in the same way, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, and vinegar, and warm oil, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water, or cooked apple peelings, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped. Then cure it as long as it takes to heal; and once swelling appears in the throat other than the two almonds, then scrape them both in the same way as the first two.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside the throat, to be specific a small tonsil abscess; and I had well closed the whole throat so that the woman could not exhale because the passage was obstructed, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she stayed like this for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that I had put in two drains through the two openings of its birth.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then at once and put a cord in one of the openings, then the pus flowed out, and there came forth a great portion of blood; then I reinserted the rest through the other opening of its birth, and I opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that I put the cord into the abscess, and some part of it came out, and only a little bit of blood came out; and thus was obstructed the passage of the throat for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut away from that abscess over long time; and the abscess grew again and filled the space that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large; at that point I covered it up and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts, and I knew only what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the urine
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eyelid swells upwards to the eye and it is inflamed and it is long, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under the eyebrow and round, then it is called "eyelid".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured in the manner that we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the boil is quieted down, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to lance it; and that which is round assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or of a fusse color or black, then it is necessary to cut out the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, concerning its shape and length, that you cause the patient to sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument which we made note of previously; then insert the needle into the eyelid, and pull the thread under, and lance with the two instruments which I mentioned in the incision of the almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you should not cover up too soon the superfluity that is outside the natural term; for if you cover it up more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said about the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about covering, then you must use an instrument at the cautery for the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is hot hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your vein, and then presses the tongue on the instrument which we said of in the chapter on cautery, and fills with live hot water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in the application of this instrument, by which it is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a head of hair or some kind of stick to hold the medicine, just like a spoon's handle, and place the instrument on top of the medicine in the urethra; and have the patient sit comfortably with his chest up, so that the saliva and mucus from his mouth flow into the medicine inside, but not down to the throat or the wound. Then take your hand and press the medicine onto the urethra for the amount of time equal to half an hour, until you see it turn black and the irritation from the medicine is calmed; and if you need to, take some cotton and wrap it around a tool, and moisten the cotton with medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton in the tube on top, until the cotton gets warm inside the urethra. And do this often, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry out, and after 4 or 5 days. And if you need to re-start the cauterization of the medicine, start again, and after that, clear out the area around the urethra with cotton soaked in butter, and clean up anything around the medicine; and be careful not to burn yourself with cold water, and be cured with gargling until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization, and if it is cured through fumigation in this manner, take camphor, yarrow, origanum, rue, chamomile, and wormwood, and gather all or some of these herbs together in one pot, and put oil in the pot, and make it boil. The pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot have a hollow instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or lead, and one of the stones should be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the cord as long as the eye is mummified; after it recurs often as long as the eye dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things occur; and never do this unless at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cord and place inside the head of the patient an egg-beater or quill, so that the mouth of the patient will not be too hot; for the egg-beater or quill does not allow the vapor to bother the mouth, and it is a good cure together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times one has seen it to be at the throat or the spine of a fish, or nothing at all; so you must try what you see and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see what the thing is; and what does not appear and is stuck in the throat, it's necessary that you make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps it will expel the bad thing through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of nail, or a root of lettuce, or one quarter of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes up, it will be cured, and you'll have done better; and if it doesn't come out from what we've said, then take a instrument of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted upwards. Be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest everything goes wrong or you push the bone inside; and it's better if the patient themselves puts the instrument in, for they will know if the thing is being expelled; if they put it down, or pull it out at the entire instrument equally, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! La première partie du texte semblait décrire une technique de traitement médical pour une affaissement ou un blocage à l'échelle des poumons, et maintenant il semble que le sujet soit la "sansue" (ou plutôt, la sève) de la gorge. Je n'ai pas d'informations claires sur ce que pourrait être cette "sansue", mais je suppose qu'il s'agit d'un terme médical anachronique qui désignait une sorte de liquide ou de flux issu de la gorge.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the blood is medicine by itself, as I have said in the division, through the cure of medications; and when that does not help, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun, after you have pressed his tongue with the instrument which I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the pus, then strip it away with a small hook or with fine pincers that are worth for such things.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't work, then take a horsehair cord and insert it into the throat of the patient, then insert the tip of the hot iron into the cord and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if fever grips the patient every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move the head back and forth often; and as soon as the pus feels the water, he will spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if he does not spit as we have said, then suffume the patient with assafetida, at the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, because it will purge soon.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is such that you take a pot in which there are glowing coals and it is covered with a cloth pierced with many holes in the middle, and in one of those perforations is the key of the instrument; then you throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the pipe into their mouth and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not come out but comes up to the nose; and now the sweat will fall. And if it does not fall, then you repeat the fumigation many times. And let the patient be thirsty and eat bitter things and suchlike, and do not let them drink water; and then it is necessary that they pass urine through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	It seems that the text you provided is a medieval medical text, likely from the 13th or 14th century. The language and style are characteristic of Old French, specifically the Middle French dialect.
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscess are similar in appearance to one another according to what is remembered hereafter from this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two kinds of them, one being similar to itself, and that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for places where they are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscess of the head is other than that of the fundament, and the abscess of the joints in the flesh is other than that which comes into joints, and each should have its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses which should not be pierced until the boil is dead according to its completion; and if there are of such kinds that it is necessary to pierce when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, like an abscess that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one lets them be until they are rotten around them, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint become corrupted, by which it is a cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it be dead, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the fundament, so that when one pierces it while still dead; and it does not behoove you to pierce an abscess that has become hard without digestion being completed, lest that which is near the fundament rot inward and become a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for piercing an abscess that is dead according to completion, and it is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the quieting of the movement and inflammation of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the perforation where it depends more on the location of the abscess, and where it opens into a cavity; and the piercing should be made with a long instrument, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there are no folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who have swollen, by displacement of that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the fatty area, it is necessary that you leave the incision so long as it becomes confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body of the venom will be drawn out and it will be filled with much foul matter; and perhaps the lips and the deepest part of it will become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that are pierced in accordance with the length of the body, according to as the member needs it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions in small abscesses, and small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many splits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses which need the knife, and a bandage; when it is become so as the cloth becomes loose, and is relaxed, then it is necessary to make just like one does with babies: and if there are those that are split in three angles, and if there are those whose incision is made like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the groin; and if there are such as which a round cut is made, and other cuts and shapes of bandage.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who does not have a head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary that you thoroughly pierce it; and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has swollen greatly and you pierce it, do not pull out all of the pus in that hour, but pull out a part; then stop the abscess up to the next day, then pull out something again from there; do this repeatedly many times, great by great, until the pus comes out entirely; likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or women bearing, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pulse beats sometimes with the issue of pus, that by chance the patient dies, and you are not aware.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound bleeds, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it's a clean cut, then dress it with linen or old cotton; and if it's large abscesses, and there are many pustules, then it is necessary that you sew in each one a suture so they come together against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have bound it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or rags of linen without moisture, and tie until the third day; then remove it, and care for it with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs at your work, then administer hot and cold water easily, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the site of the bleeding several times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then administer governance and treatment, and the powders that I have said are in the hands of the leeches in this book, and if it is summer time, and the site or abscess is most swollen, so it is necessary that you put on damp tents and drapery with wine and hot oil; and if it is winter, and the site is fatty, so it is necessary that you put on damp drapery in water and oil, or in cold wine, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess and the discharge and cure it, as is necessary, until they are healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is necessary to understand universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must go before the treatments of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	swellings
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where tumors come from the head, they are small abscesses, and in manner like spider webs, just as the nesting of a hen, and there are many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fatty and such tumors where there is moisture also like boils; and if there are such that are hard and stony when cut, and there is no doubt that the surgeon will make it contrarily.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the abscess are that you try all instruments which are called "entromissor", from which the form comes later, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then let it be opened on top of a long (thing).
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape it without leaving anything of the skin that contains that moisture, for it comes back again if you leave anything behind; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if there is any; if not, in water and lye, and anoint the wound, and let it be just until the next day; and those who are residing on night will run those who are dwelling of nits.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then reapply the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain by night; then heal the wound with ointment as seems fitting, until it is clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess remains full of pus, cut it according to this form, from long; and cast out your needles, and scrape off all around, and put all your treatment of drawing out pus behind the shirt where it lies; and if the artery causes you contrary, do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do with the abscess if it is hard and tough, and of cutting and of healing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on top of the abscess that is hard and moist, if it is lighter, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are some of these abscesses or swellings that have no moisture, and I found one such abscess on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a hardened stone, sharp and white, and it could not break; and if anyone had attempted to burst any of them, they would have made him as much pain as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.
