In other abscesses coming from the head, such as those that come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at its most dependent position so that pus can exit; and it is treated as needed.
des scrophules	Of swellings.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come to other parts of the body, and are foul-smelling, and are intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly located within its own side, as the swelling and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and similar things are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some boils that contain moisture, and there are some malignant ones that do not want to obey treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that one then you see of good disposition to touch, and is similar in color to the flesh, and is not red on the neck or at the artery or channel, and is not deep; it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape off all parts, and take the two lips of the boil with your fingers, if you need them, as we have said about abscesses of the head; and pull it out slowly and slowly, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, nor is it the spatula edge or incision, that the hands escape, and do not see too far ahead, that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put vitriol powder in the wound, or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound becomes soft, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, if it returns to your work, until you have completed it; then inquire of your sworn oath whether any small scrofulous matter remains, and cut them out and scrape them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, then it is not necessary for you to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with strong double thread, and let it hang down, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton steeped in Egyptian oil, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cover the whole scrofula with ointment, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then there is no remainder of excess because of the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that hold excess, pierce it where it is most sore; and pierce thus as the one before mentioned, downwards, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that what remains of corruption corrupts; and when the wound is well cleansed, apply a salve of oil drawing off flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	Squince.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones said and spoke of the cutting out of the throat; but I never saw in our land one who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squince, it is necessary that the cut of the throat which is called "epiglote" be severed; and that one not help by these things, because all the veins and the pulse of the patient are at those who have apoplexy warm in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two parts.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pulse, it is necessary to cut out the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four with a small incision through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision as much as the siffac allows, not in the cartilage; and those parts are convenient for the section of the epiglottis because there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is timid, it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat to all the nape, then cut the flesh as far as comes to the chin; and let out the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then close the lymphatic vessel, just as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein of the chin which jumps forth through the place that is broken, and by the failure of the voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed that one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the skin and sew it all together except for the cartilage; then administer medications which make flesh grow, until it be healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albusimus (a medieval Latin expression meaning "we have sufficiently explained") says that one should not do this just so far as the throat is completely stopped and the patient is judged to be dying, and the wound is giving out pus.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglottis for what the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus it is guarded against death; and because they commanded the ancients to leave the wound open as long as the malignity of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four And then they commanded that the wound be stitched up and cured, as long as it was cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took the dagger, and stuck it in her throat, and cut out part of the channels from the womb; and I was called to cure her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had come out of it, and I saw well that she had not cut too deep nor gone far into the throat, and the veins were coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and cured her so that she was sound; and it came to pass that the young lady spoke as if with a sore throat, and returned to her normal condition; therefore I say that in cutting out the epiglottis there should not be fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of jasper, and it is common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; or natural which has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is in two ways, because one is similar to fat nodules, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it does not seem good to work with fire unless on the one that is small, and prove and search the entire surrounding: if you find it just like I mentioned as fat, and cannot be drawn out in any way, then cut it, just as one cuts nodules, and treat it entirely with its cloak; if there is not a single thread, then search thoroughly, and cure it as it should be, so that it is perfectly sound.
des nous	of the nodules.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are ours, of which I will say all similarities; and now it is necessary that I say the entire difference that is between them and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is hot and feverish, as long as the inflammation has not passed, and the purulence is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the nout there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it swells, which is its own sac and is in accordance with the colour of the body, and begins as well as a boil, and becomes big; and they are according to two likenesses, either fatty, or moist, and much of them are so coloured as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to cure the nodule, that you probe and examine it first with all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to what its form will be, whether it is a head or a pouch which comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of the incision of the abscesses of the nout is that you take or the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two needles back and forth, as much as you know that the instruments have pierced to the core, then as it be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the instrument, and be careful lest it burst forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes across the cartilage, regardless of its color, do it just as I have said about other abscesses; and if after introducing the instrument there is no moisture, know that it is fatty, so then do it in a cross shape, and take hold of it with pincers, and scrape it lightly from each part and towards the heart where it lies, then you will pull it out healthy with the new; and if you cannot pull it out healthy, then pull it out by pieces as much as there remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there remains nothing, the wound will return many times; and if there remains a small part, but the blood grieves it, then plug the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and bind the wound tightly, and put on soothing things over the hot abscess, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the wound is large, then cut off the two edges of the wound, and cure what rots the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the sore is stubborn or you are in a hurry, then apply vitriol powder to the wound, and leave it for two or three days until the pus has come out, and the inflammation of the blood has subsided; then return to cutting out what remains of the nodule.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here is the line-by-line translation:
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of tumors are of many kinds, like this: great ones, middling ones, and small ones; and there are tumors with two kinds of horns in three ways, as well; and there are tumors with three horns, and also of three kinds; and there are tumors with two horns, and a tumor with only one horn, but are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are cutting, and there are some that do not cut further than one part, from which we scrape the nails, so that the vein or nerve is not touched; and among these are introduced ones in the form of gauze, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they come in three ways: great, small, and middling, as you see; and one should only use them for a solid place, such as legs, arms, breasts, armpits, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling nail scrapers, according to this form, with which we stem blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes in the place where there are cuts of veins and arteries, and sometimes it comes out according to this large shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Some times the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts; and remain swollen and ugly, and whoever wants to cure them, should do so according to this shape from line b to line g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then skin the fat, and fill the wound with medicine issuing in char, then sew up the two lips of the wound at costure, and heal it until it is sound; and if the breast leans down, and is swollen for its size as happens to women, so make it in two folds above, by two similar incisions; of which one should be joined to the other at the end of each and both, so that the greater line contains the lesser according to this shape from line b. to the line g.; then skin the leather which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said of costure and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is sound; and if it is not sound, or the incision has not been made entirely, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the clotting of blood, so you must fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it melts the remaining fat and flesh, then heal it until it is sound.
des apostemes des asselles	the nodules of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These nodules that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas or carbuncles, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who are moist-affected should be bandaged according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g..
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the nodule has been emptied, then fill the wound with fresh cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with soothing oil as needed until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the nodule is of a similar nature to carbuncles, then treat it as we said for incisions of carbuncles, and if the wound fills with pus again, then apply cauterization as we said before.
de la routure de l’artere	the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is bruised, and the skin above it is sewn up, then many times an abscess forms, and just as often there is swelling of the vein and abscess; and if one knows this when it's due to the artery, the abscess is long in depth inside; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels hard; and when it's because of the vein, it's swollen far away from its appearance; and it's foolishness to cover up this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and elbows and neck and in many other places, and it's very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must then take out the cautery, and that one who is head-affected also needs to be treated; and in him who has a swelling due to an artery, make a cut on top of the skin long enough; then work the knife along the stitches, and carefully separate the artery from the threads, until it is discovered; then put under the vein an awl, and make it pierce all the way to the other side, and hold the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have instructed you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then sew up the place between the two threads with a tampon so that the blood is not coming out, and be released the abscess; then put back on the bandage that had been taken off, until the thread falls; then cure with ointments suitable to those things, until they are healed; and if the abscess is due to an incision of the vein, you must mark with your hand what you can extract from the abscess onto all the skin, then put in the awl under the place you hold with your hand, and make it pierce, and there will be two threads, so that you pull it out from the other side; then tie up the abscess, as I have said to you, or tie one of the ends of the thread to each of the two holes of the cautery; and if you doubt that the pus is not coming out, put in another awl through all the thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first awl, and hold the threads in four places; then bandage up the abscess until the superfluities come out, then bandage the superfluity of the skin and leave what is tied together; then put on a damp cloth soaked in vinegar and oil, then give him cures with tents and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	the nodules of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also like nodules that come to the artery and the vein, nodules also come to the nerves when they are irritated or due to excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more often in the shoulders and knees and everywhere where there are joints, and it is one of the grievous abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the flesh, and it is in many dispositions without pain; and when you hold it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely within the body, but beneath the skin; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor upwards or downwards, and that which is in joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps there would be contraction; and he who is in the head or in the forehead, apply a poultice to the splintile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, tie it with forceps and cut it in its root; and if it is great, suspend it to the navel, and scrape it, then cauterize it and sew up the wound to the seam, and take care of him until he is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large, hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There occurs sometimes in bellies and not elsewhere the thing, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms; and the roots are fine, and the head is big; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I have seen one man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thin root, and were already cracked open, and were always moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied them and found that the one weighed 18 ounces, and the other 6 ounces; and the work in incising it is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist and has a fine root; if you cut into it with a spatula large, and let the cautery be by fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart. Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an infected nodule, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the pus has been emptied out.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or rupture of an abscess on the belly and in some of the parts that are like other ruptures, or from blood flowing out of veins or arteries according to what is mentioned before, or from windiness; and if it is because of the rupture of an abscess and the issue of pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and easy to have different issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is much more varied, and when one presses it with their hands it swells up, and then goes back down, and perhaps it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and due to great exertion.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and you will clearly know when you press on it with your hand, and it does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, it will show by these signs the abscess large and hard, and filled with a quantity; and if it is due to flatulence, it is soft to touch, and the operation is that you must see if the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary for you to leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowels, then it is necessary for you to command the patient to strain his urine, and have him stretch out straight, then sign with a mark all around the belly; then command him to lie down soon between your hands, then go around the place that you marked with a straight line, then extend half of the abscess above to the great incision; then bind it around with a strong thread or a cord of thick silk firmly, and let the ends be well tied; then operate on the extended half of the abscess, and put your right index finger inside, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught in the thread, then loosen it, and put the intestine back into the belly; and if you find the bowels, then take them up with the incision, and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery or vein goes against you, then go slowly around, then come back to your operation and take two needles, and put two strong threads on them, and put the two needles through what you made in a cross shape that you made pierce; then tighten the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it has formed pus, and discard the dead flesh by itself; or you cut it when it is softened and formed pus, then treat the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as needed, and close the place.
dou chancre	It seems like we've reached a section of text that doesn't follow the previous instructions on how to treat an abscess.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division that cancerous sores are similar to ulcers, and how one must work on them with medicines, and how one must avoid treating with fire; and we say that cancer begins in the groin, and great caution is necessary in its cure, and the ancients said that when a cancer is in place where it can be cut out like a sore on the breast, or on the armpit, or on similar places, and you should remove it all at the beginning; and when it is large and old, then you must not approach it, for I have never seen one cured; nor has anyone ever been healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once with black cohosh; then let them recover if they are manifestly full of blood; then prepare the patient, i.e. a good place to perform the operation; then throw out your knives or cancer, and scrape off all parts, and leave nothing behind; and let the blood congeal completely, and squeeze the place well with your hand or on some thing, and if the bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein is contrary to what you expect, cauterize it as long as the blood is stopped; then cure them with another cure until they are healed.
de ydropisie	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And they shall cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	With a point and always not so sharp that it can come up to the intestines when you insert it and cannot hurt them; then see if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if it is necessary that you cut upwards from three fingers on the right of the navel; and if it's because of the disease of the liver, then your incision will be on the left of three fingers; and if it's due to the spleen, then it will be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluous things do not run towards that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument and insert it, and lift your hand as much as the spatula between the skin and the flesh as when scraping to the quantity of an fingernail or around it; then pierce the flesh until the spatula comes to its natural place, and that is the seat of the water; then take out the instrument and insert this tool which is the shape:

At the top is the alemele, so that when the instruments come to the water, they descend now on the instrument; empty then half or a third part, for if you empty more than is necessary at this hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of their spirit of the arm, or they will faint, or they will approach death; but empty according to the quality of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtuous liquid of the patient signify, and his hairs; then take the instrument and hold the water, and it is now held by the cork that stops the perforation which is on the syringe, of which I spoke, so that you pierce in this manner; then return the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw out a small quantity of water; do this every day, and beware of overflowing until it remains but a little drop of water.

de l’estopement de la verge	of the strangling of the penis.

Those who do not have the ulcer in its place are obstructed, for none are born with an ulcer at the head of the penis, so that they cannot urinate before they lift their penis up; and cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach as far as the margin, and this is a bad disease.

And the manner of performing this operation is that the patient lies on his back most of the time, with the head of the penis and scrotum as big as a goose's egg, so that the opening can come out in its proper place; and he should be kept from bleeding which often comes, and if it does, it should be stopped by someone who knows how to stop bleeding, and care for the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of boils on the penis.

de la circoncision	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the loosening of continuity like other wounds; nonetheless when we do this work of our free will and properly with children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the most gentle for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children because they do not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the greatest part of masters and sirs who used to do circumcision around one year, and in good health, and with full strength; it was rejected by children because they had two scabs, and perhaps if you scrape off the top one it would leave the lower one underneath.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it heals by scraping, and the pain is doubled, and with the cleansing which is around one year isn't sure the point of the member; and with the cleansing of the nail perhaps escapes the iron, and runs the work, and many times are born thus they don't need cleansing and I want that.

de hernie carnouse	It appears that the text is describing a medieval surgical procedure for treating a type of hernia.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A waterbag is nothing other than an assembly of mucous or white mucus, which is under the skin of the testicles that contain the egg; and it is called "mucous", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the testicle, so one thinks it is another testicle; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white mucous we mentioned; and it has no harm.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the origin of this waterbag is weakness that comes to the testicles, and it spreads that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And at any time if it comes to percussion over the scrotum, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a color declining towards yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or transparent white, and so on; and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is whitish such as we have said, it is the abscess swollen, I think long like the shape of an egg, and does not open up the scrotum, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if he has moisture in the proper cloth, it is the abscess swollen with one part of the yolk, and because of this we think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white shining surface, he feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, try it at all four quarters, for what shape it makes before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to these things then, that come after the introverted quarter, judge what is inside.

And when we heal it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be anointed according to our power and the replenishment of his body; then place him on his back, on something not too high, and put a lot of cloths under him; then sit down beside him on his left side, and instruct the servant to sit at his right side, and extend the instrument towards one of the two bones of the penis; then take the scalpel lightly, and cut the skin of the penis from the long part up to the root, and let the incision be entirely straight while cutting the skin of the penis until it is white, and carefully scrape off the scab according to our power; then pierce the whole whitish part with a needle to make a large hole, and extract all the blood, and then place stitches, and lift up the scab; and do not touch the bone of the penis, but only the scab; cut out entirely or in pieces at once the flesh from under it so carefully that if you don't cut well, the blood will return; and if the swelling gets too big for your work, take it back to its place when you have completed the work of the scab; then assemble the two leaves of the skin of the penis with a suture, then cure him just like other wounds, until he is healed.

de l’aposteme des coions	From the swelling of the testicles.

de hernie carnouse	It appears that the text is describing a medieval surgical procedure for treating a type of hernia.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this place I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the treatment with iron.

de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Concerning the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum becomes soft in some men, because the testicles that are inside become softened, and it is easy to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to treat it, that the sick person lies on his back, and then stitches the softened skin over the natural skin; then sew together the two edges with a single suture, and if you want, stitch first the excess of softened skin at three or four firm stitches; then sew between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and have the thread come out.
dou chastrement	Concerning punishment.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and for this reason it would please me if I did not speak of it at all in this book; and there is no need except for two purposes: one is that the physician should know how to respond when asked about a cure; and the other, because we often have need of castrating certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then take them with your hand, until they come back together and you can no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the punishment of branding: it is necessary that you stain the animal, and press the skin of the genitals against your left hand, then tie the suspender, and strike above each horn with a hammer, when you have well cleaned them; and let there be no thick sap or subtle sap which is over the vessels; and this manner of punishment is more efficacious than that made by attraction, for it stays by chance some thing from the genitals, because of which the animal desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	those who have a mixed sex (i.e., hermaphrodites)
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners in men: the one if it is that between the two testicles appears as well as the shape of a woman's nature, or there are hairs, and sometimes flows urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the thigh as well as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The cure for a boil and for woman is such that you cover the swollen parts altogether, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, men whose urine shoots through the skin of their groin have no cure.
de la tentigene	of the unicorn
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A swelling is a swollen part on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you mark the superfluity of the swelling on your hand or on fingernails, and cover it lightly; and do not go too deep in so that blood does not come out, then cure it with another treatment until it is healed; and there is another boil that arises at the mouth of the uterus, and apply it, and by chance it bursts forth, and it resembles the shape of a cow, and for this reason they called it in ancient times "cow sickness".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cover it, as we have said the incision, and heal it until it is sound.
de erratique	It seems you're reading from an old medical text. "De Erratique" doesn't appear to be a clear term, but I can try to translate the surrounding context.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	There is an irregularity if the nature of the woman is not pierced, or the holes are small; and it is natural by birth, or by accident from disease that has come upon her; or it is from a tumor attached to the intestines, or a subtle or thick abscess, made in front or in the sides or beneath, or whatever it may be; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having flowers (i.e. children); and knowledge of this comes by looking at the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is nearby in appearance, it should be cut to your elbow or down to the rib.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle abscess and it is nearby to the navel, you should hurry and cut into it: put both hands index-finger together, and have the woman sit on her back, spread out her legs; then press the two fingers firmly until the subtle abscess bursts, and be over the swelling; then take lint, moisten in oil, and place on the navel, and let the woman stay at home each day, so she may not close.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the styptic is hard and thick, so you must steep the roots in vinegar similar to the leaves of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from blood, suspend it at the elbow and strike it; and have bleeding medicines for blood, such as aconite, dragon's blood, aloes, and yolk together in abundance; then apply a linen bandage wide enough that the wound cannot close; and thus let it be long-lasting, and then provide a tent of dry linen; and then be cured with other remedies until you are healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the thigh comes blood, it is necessary to strike it according to this manner, unless there are encysted abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an encysted abscess in the thigh, one should not apply fire.
des emorroides	Piles (hemorrhoids)
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which normally and commonly occur, and when hemorrhoids are old they become a boil; and we have said in the section about them their similarities, and signs, and I will say here those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and a thrombus, when they are deeply located in the rectum, and they do not appear to feel anything, except for treatment with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the entrance of the rectum, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then set the uterus on fire with pincers, and cauterize its roots, then powder over medicine that restrains blood, such as assafoetida and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the bed for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes from it, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and asphalt, and make into a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he is stricken (i.e. hit), it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him feel a draft of bloodsuckers on the back and shoulders without hurting him; then take linen and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, then heal the place with ointment until it is sound; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a sharp headache, so you should cover it as I said of the boil; and then heal it until it is sound.
des apostemes de la marris	Je comprends que vous voulez me poser une question plus spécifique.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come to the navel, such as ulcers and pus-filled abscesses and herpetic blisters and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes on the breast; which is not of the abscesses that boil. And if you want to know how to work with iron, look and see if the abscess is swollen at its beginning of coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then don't rush to pierce it, but let it cool until the pain is calmed; and then make the patient sit on a stool, and have two small stools for them to recline against, and support their back and put their legs apart at the far side of the leg; and have their thighs spread out, and place their arms under their knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then proceed to give the patient an anesthetizing draught towards the right side, and bring in the instrument with which one works on the mouth of the breast, from which this form comes later; and it is necessary that when you see bringing in this instrument, you fix the first thread inside so as to know the depth of the breast, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and will not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the breast with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt them; and it is necessary that they put the cone of the instrument above, and that you tie the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and it is made soft by hand, then you must cover at the head, with linen sheet let loose; and when the bowstring is empty, then you must put in the wound damp cloths moistened in rose oil or green oil dry; and put the cloths above the wound at the bottom of the mattress, and put a clean damp linen cloth on top of the mattress and on the pillow, and after 2 days of ointment coming as is to those, until it is healed; and once raise up the mattress and the wound by purging with water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and aristolochia long been cooked; and then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the mattress, then you must beware of cooking with iron, but heal it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first at the birth that the woman knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs which are that when you see the woman advancing forward and wanting to smell the air: then hastens the child to come out quickly; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue comes under its head, and the placenta with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her stomach, so that the child comes out quickly; because when it ascends above its head, the placenta comes with it, and the mother is made clean of its superfluities by good cleansing; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Because it sometimes comes out above its feet and comes quickly outside the body or through the head or hands, or it comes out of the stomach, or side, and is converted by chance over the neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the woman to be wise and subtle in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures about how one should help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out under its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth easily, and her strength is weak, let her sit on a chair, or women hold her; and bring her some oil of olive or fenugreek cooked, and then put the midwife between her shoulders a small spatula with this shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the membrane, and cut to her finger so that the moisture which is inside may come out; and touch the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman a suppository of fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her press and strain with condiments, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands emerge, it is necessary that you gently manipulate them back and forth; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a stool, and raise her feet up high; then lower the stool to the ground, and grasp the woman so she does not move; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife that is placed before you, and extract the child, and manipulate them evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the infant begins to stand on its feet, it must be supported upwards; and then turn it slowly, little by little, until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them out little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	But if he jumps up as high as his hips, instruct him to bend over and make himself sweat with effort; but if he jumps high, then it is God's will.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he is not further as we have said, then turn him little by little until he is according to the natural shape.

Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not jump high as we have said, then take muskellunge of the river, and oil of sassafras, and melted gum, and grind it all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in a hot bath down to the lower ribs; and when she is moistened underneath, then put the cologne of myrrh on her and place it under, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the stool, then make her sweat and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for now the infant will jump.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from between her legs.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the infant comes in this form, then put the pillow under his hands small and small; then be careful on his neck, and let the feet hang down, and be bent over the bed; and fold his hands small and small, and then take them up to his belly, and remove the cushions underneath, so that it is prepared downwards; and if the infant does not cry, then take its feet and bend it correctly, then bend the belly upwards, then put your hands; and hold the baby small and small; and instruct the woman to hold herself until the infant emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	The issue of the child who comes out too wide is a hand during birth.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer. It is necessary that the patient takes hold of his hand, then turns it slowly and carefully, and when it is level, puts on the natural soothing ointment of aloes and oil, as we have said, and then instructs it to move slowly; and when you have done this, has her sit on a stool, and instructs it to grasp; and she must take hold.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	by the same method for the entire second stage (of labor).
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way to the second birth, then cut the second membrane at your nail, until the moisture is empty; and if the afterbirth hangs on her face and on her neck, then cut from below, so that it does not remain, and kill the afterbirth; then put the child inside, as long as you have put it in as it should be, and command the woman to take hold once: then let it go easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes none are born, three or four at a time; and it is not an extraordinary thing, and this often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Twins are an unusual thing and do not live at all if they can be named; I know them to be multiplied, and they are severed by the womb that divides them, which is tied to the navel; and sometimes they issue naturally like us all sinews, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue grievously, if the treatment is as we have said, and the belly is subtle, and does it quickly and lightly what she does; and do so that it moves towards health.
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than fifteen, and are completely shaped in the form of an infant by the measurement of the wise God, and it is necessary that the belly knows everything about this, for perhaps a similar thing happens to them; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman who has lost her child or is in labor, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to intervene with your hands; so you must know if the woman is of good health and does not have an accident or fear of death; so the woman should be sitting on her back, and her head inclined downward, and her legs lifted; and the minister will apply a poultice of two parts, or she will be tied to the bed since she has not been treated in the descent of the child;
