then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oils with muscillage of aloes and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the hands of the midwife with these oils and these muscillaiges; then insert them into the vagina lightly, then let go or she will put the onces in places that are convenient to it, and pay attention if the child is descending onto its head; if so, plant the onces in their holes or in her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or under the beard or in the navel or near the ribs, and if the descent is on the feet, then prick or pinch and tie the onces to the sides; and it should attach the once to its right hand, and put the crown between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the once into any of these places that we have said, as long as it will come out empty; and this is the shape of the once:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then take a thread of linen, or if you have silk on hand, use it so that the extraction is equal; and then stretch them equally by moving from one side to the other, in order to get out, and let the stitches be fine so that they can hold, as here is the form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains a part, take some of its fat and anoint the ball with it, put it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if none remains, then move this thread or more above its place, and do so until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other and it cannot be brought back due to the tightening, then you must wrap a cloth over this, until it comes out completely; then bandage it on the joint of the heel or at the ankle, and similarly do this with the other hand, and for both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's jaw is thick and it is tense in the outlet, or it has a sharp angle assembled, you should push the spatula spine between your fingers, and make the jaw and extract the angle; or you will turn to the instrument which is called "almidach", from which the shape comes with instruments or treatise that follows this; and thus do the same for the child who naturally has a thick jaw; and then pull on the bones with pliers, and if the jaw jumps out and it holds at the forceps, so it is split, as long as the moisture that is in the outlet comes out; and if it cannot come out, you will cut by pieces at the joints that you can; and if it is swollen under the ribs or belly, you should pierce until the moisture drains.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the baby is on its feet, it's a gentle delivery, and the approach to the mouth of the womb is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is tense in the belly or chest, you should pull it out to the unfolded cloth on the hand; and make the belly or chest, as long as the moisture that is there drains; and if the other members are cut away, and the jaw remains, you should put the needle of the probe deep into the marrow, and pull it up to the mouth of the marrow; then you should put in one or two, and pull out; and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed due to hot abscess that has come there, you do not need to work on it, but rather apply moist and greasy things; and make a poultice, and so too with mild waters and soothing.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the hernia is above the navel, and you can place it level, then give him the same treatment as we have said for a living child; and if you cannot do so, then cut it out with pieces, and leave nothing of the cord.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the abscess comes to a head as we have said for those that come in the groin; and if there is bleeding from the incision, it should be put in cool water restraining it, and give him other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a dead baby had been placed, then she became pregnant with another on top of it, and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time the swollen abscess came on the cheek, and swelled so much that it burst open, and began to cause great inflammation.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned to the cure, and I thought for long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a poultice of great attraction, and from it came bones, and after some days another ones.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because the abdomen has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I saw the wound, and in it were many bones, until the woman was better; and the woman lived a long time thus, and still had a small piece of bone out of place; and I do not remember writing this chapter except for this reason, that when a master finds an unusual thing, he should know how to treat it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the flesh to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	There comes then the shape of the scribe, by whom we write the books; and two turnings in the two pages of the two columns.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Whatever the horns are more subtle than the rim of the cauldron, and they are made of ebony or beech; and the mouth of the shaft must be two fingers wide, and the edge of the tree two hands long and a half; and between the two hinges there are two fastenings of the same wood, which are firm in one and the other, half a hand long or a little more; and these two fastenings are inserted into the mouth of the mortar to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of wood from ebony or beech, according to the shape of pliers; and it has two hinges, as you see, a hand long, and two fingers wide; and when you want to open the mortar with all the instrument, so place the woman on a bed, her feet raised and legs apart, then insert the two hinges together in the mortar, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand with all the instrument, as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the size that you want to open the mouth of the mortar, until the woman achieves what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	It seems that the conversation has shifted to a more general topic.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument if you have not prepared it, for its needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then cause her to yawn with condensation, and restrain her hands on her mouth and nose; and if she falls for this, it's well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, and make an opening or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the belly, such as calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne and centoire; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or steeped in water above the fire; then put a cord or opening on the pot, and the other head in the mouth of the belly, and let her yawn so that the vapors come inside the belly; then cause her to yawn, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine jumps out hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not pass, instruct the nurse to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or almond milk, and then insert it into the nature, and seek out the secondine; and when she has found it, take hold of it and stretch it little by little straightly, so that the belly does not tear at the extraction; but you must move it slightly to the right and left, and then draw; and it will come and discharge itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is too tightly closed, we have said the treatment for hiccoughing and the fumigation of herbs; and if she does not take that which we have said, you must beware lest you do further harm; but it behooves what is at the mouth of the womb that you tie it to the navel of the woman, then anoint her with tetrafarmacical ointment; thus will she be restored and put right, and come to health. But nevertheless, when she does this there comes bad odour to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary to do fumigations advisable for this: none of the ancients have proven that fumigation with lettuce and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman at retention of flowers and secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like looking at a similar thing to a cord, and one places the head of it finely in its nature, and the knobs large over the fire; and there are fumigations above the coals, and the lice until they are consumed, and then another comes again.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation (of the uterus)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but rather it has been stopped by a subtle ligament: so then the midwife must make her pierce that ligament at its proper place, and let her not pierce with a spatula tip, and tie the bandage in such a way that she does not touch it; then put on damp flax soaked in wine and oil, then cure with ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not set, then put or make a poultice with a string, and let it be on for many days, and remove it when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And when this swelling comes of a sudden from a wound or an abscess; then it is necessary to cover it immediately: and if it be cured, as we have said about the poultice.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula of the fundament (or anus)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that come from under the fundament are nodule-shaped and grow outward that come from near the fundament forward, or in the cleft between the two parts, if one has a fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works, and even more moist pus comes out white or subtle yellow, and at times these fistules perforate; and they are known by those that come out with discharge or vomiting when the patient does evacuation, and possibly a worm jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if one has fistulas that pierce just to the bladder and just to the middle of the penis; and reach just to the joint of the thigh, and just to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula that pierces to the fundament, and does not pierce: take your index finger or fundament, and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has tortuosity, then insert a thin piece of linen or horsehair as long as you feel the end with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no passage of pus, or wind, or worm, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces down to the bladder or down to the urethra, then the urine comes out and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces just to the joint of the groin, then the thread comes out just to its place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain around it, then know that it will burst again, and does not benefit from medicine or binding by ointment; and in these piercing fistulas there is no sure cure except labor, and vanity of foolish doctors who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that case which is not a piercing and is not ancient, I have hope of recovery by iron, as I have tried it, and the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift up his legs until they are above his thighs, and have his thighs inclined to his belly; then insert an iron tent or a copper one if there is tortuosity, as long as you know the tent comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should insert your second and third fingers into it; if it is then pierced by the tent, and it is discovered where you feel between your finger and the skin or flesh, then know that it is a piercing; if not done so, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can well heal some, but it is rare; and the aid that one does there, if it is, is to scorch the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before; and insert it hot into the fistula, until it comes near the fundament; and do this two or three times, as long as you know those charred parts are burned, which are similar to a bird's feather; and then cure with moist tents in grease, as long as that char is coming out; then cure with ointment drawing flesh and soldering.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is so, for it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the abscess bursts, but does not pierce just to the core which is at the base, and between your skin and the abscess there is a thick layer of fat or flesh, and you see the fistula coming out from under the layer of fat; then cut away from the beginning of the fistula, and push it ahead of the abscess, and then apply the cautery afterwards, as far as it comes to the head of the abscess; and the abscess will be delivered, and it will dry up; then scrape off those parts of the flesh that resemble a bird's feather, and none should remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound swells up, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicinal water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery assembles two bad things: that is to say, the scorching of these attached flesh parts, and the searing of blood and the drying out of moisture; then cure moisted boils in mud or in cheese broth, until the place discharges pus, and let loose the burnt flesh into the pus; then cure the wound with ointments that soothe inflamed hard flesh, and are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it has been restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes right down to the fundament and is far from the body, then stick your finger into the fundament and inspect it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the boil, and it is between two or under the skin or flesh, where it is close to bursting, if there are no signs of fever except for hope and expectation, by administering one of the three methods: or you cauterize it just as we said, or you lance it up to the bottom, or if you can put in tents and treat it just as we first said; and do not go too deep that you cut the skin that holds the foundation, and cause an egestion by chance; then cure it, just as we said. Perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it is lanced near the bottom, either by tent or by another instrument assigned; then cleanse that foul flesh which is in the wound, as long as you can; then study to restore the wound, and remain the fistula in the part beyond the foundation: if it were a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And at any time hollow tubes are made in this manner: and is when you insert a tube into the fistula, and it is on the opposite side from the base near the skin above, so take a pierced tube at the head according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and insert one twisted thread in two, and insert the tube into all the thread in the fistula as far as it goes to the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced at the edge of the base inside, then take out the thread from that puncture, in this way as you insert your finger or base; and draw the head of the thread, and gather the two heads together, and hold one against the other, and let it be for a day or two; and hold it again, until the threads bind themselves between the two, and bleed; then treat the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it to pierce in all ways that you can, as long as it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make a hole that is too deep and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spine of the thorn from which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and split; and on the other side not, for that reason one does not bleed what one must not bleed, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the curved ones.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Wounds are according to two manners: or they are within the fundament, just like grain of resin, and there are small ones and large ones, and in a short time blood comes out, and there is one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those that are outside so have little moisture, and in a short time or a little drop of yellow bile or a little drop of blood, and have the color of the body; and the cure for those who are within the fundament, is that you command the patient to get up to rooms, until the fundament comes out on top, and they appear the root; if it hastens, and let it be taken in pincers, or you hold it at your finger, then cut into its roots; and if the unguent cannot hold because of their moistors, take them in a cloth, or in cotton, or in a piece of chamlet; and extract to your arms, then cut, and powder over hot powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize it just as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure with other cures until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, make the patient purge with purging draught and harsh for to wash what is in the fundament, so that it can come out clearly; when the patient feels it, and if the thread is coming from the fundament, it is a light cure; and is that you take them at your finger or in pincers, and cut, then cure just as we have said, until they are healed, and do not fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you bring the thread to the stitch in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it on an awl, and then pull the thread upwards and make the awl pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread around the awl together, so that they be of equal width; and hold the thread tightly, then tie the thread, and draw out the awl, and do likewise with all the others, and leave one part open for the superfluity of blood; then put on the foundation a dampened cloth in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let him lie until he has done, and when they have stopped, so cure them with ointment and other treatment, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the drying up of the fundament or fundament's opening.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying up of the fundament in the intestine, and by natural constriction, and when the sickness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you reset the tip of a splinter or on a nail the bark above, which does not let it moisten; then treat it until it becomes hard as it should be; and if it cannot harden, so renew the scraping more strongly than before, until it heals completely, and the bark falls off; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	from the flux.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance located in front of the body, and go deep inside. And at times the female finds the cold place, and feels it just like a dead mouse, and comes to all parts of the body, and especially to the hands rather than other places.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a twig from an owl's feather, or a strong goose quill, and put that twig on the mouse, so that the circle around it covers the whole mouse; then turn your hand around all of the twig until you have covered the whole mouse, and push the twig deep inside, and extract the roots of the mouse.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, then do as with a thread of silver or iron according to this shape, and make it subtle below and draw it above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that you can hold it with your fingers, and squeeze it hard. And if you see it, then burn the flux as is said in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the clyster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or gold, or molten and beaten metal, and sometimes one makes those small and large instruments according to which they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are administered in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large clyster is as follows: above wide, or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is an obstruction or the belly is bound together, just as you see, and the head of the intestine is pierced inside; and it has two holes on one side and one on the other; and it is wrapped in a bladder of animal skin or parchment with medicines, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there is a space of one finger between each hole, then insert strong thread made of twisted rope yarn in the shape of X or crossed into each hole, and assemble the belly as if it were a she-goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie the instrument to the front with a strong thread, then clisterize; and that's what forms the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the chief of the poultice with oil or hazelnut oil or egg yolk or a similar thing, then place it on lightly; then bind the ministers to his two hands together, so that he is completely still, then remove the poultice, and lift the patient's legs up high, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it seep as much as it can; and if he sleeps all night straight, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize him in the disease of purging of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it as many times as necessary until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in their foundation or abscess, so let the poultice be as subtle as for a child; and this is the shape of the subtle poultice on which the skin will be strained:
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments for hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things through which wounds are made are by the fall of stone, and cutting with sword and knife or lance or club or arrow, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, for the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from a fall on stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of a hot abscess: then make it heal with the cephalic salve right away if there is blood flow from the wound, and the salve is in contrast to the damaged part; and remove the patient's repletion of wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to heal, so its meat is lessened, and it drinks no wine, nor eats any flesh; and places on the wound, if a hot abscess comes, a moistened cotton cloth in rose oil alone, or in vinegar stiptic; and if there is no hot abscess, then places on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not been moved by air, powder, which I will say more about later; and if the ulcer has moved it, then places some ointments on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot come together by themselves, then bring them together by stitching, just as I will say about wounds of the belly, in the chapter on stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is discovered to be of the bone, and it is open and will no longer hold by just a thread, then close it; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as cooked testes and emmer, also like poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a foulness of the skin, and it is not to the bone, then close the foulness completely, and wash it clean, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped by medicine, so cut the artery; and if you find it dislodged, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and that you put in this powder which heals at once when the inflammation has subsided.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of this powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; fresh hazel wood three parts, and pound it finely, and apply the wound, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it tight, and let it alone without untying, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine as long as it is sound.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes we do this with lime alone, when we don't have incense or dragon's blood, but the inflammation has already made the wound swell.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer has moved the wound, just as it was, do not put on this powder; but apply some digesting ointments, or hairs made of barley flour mixed with water and honey, until they seep through; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the break of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is an abscess, then there is no other device than to leave the cure and not put anything restraining on it, because it harms abscesses and makes them retreat; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, because the substance of abscesses is cold, and their continuation so is with the brain, which is the highest member; but if you are skilled in medicine, such as washing with warm water and mixing with rose oil, and aloe juice washed also in warm water, and other minerals in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and tie with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and wide and full of pus, then poke them lower down; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes out, tie it up, and cauterize it when necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduit is kept so that the flesh goes, then sew up the wound on the dog's skin of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape; and then bind it astringently, and leave it for some days, and then cure with ointments of unguents until they are healed; and if the wound has made impression in the bone, then scrape it; and if there are fragments of bone, then extract them all that you can, and those that you cannot have, let them be as long as the wound festers and is discharged and clean the issue; and if the wound is fresh, then powder with the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then cure it thus as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the stab wound or cut
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look if windiness issues from the wound in the patient's armpit: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder on the wound at first hour nor bind it to keep the blood from welling up inside and going back to the heart and killing the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and tie it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient sleep above the wound for three days, or four, or more; so that spasms will not come nor evil tremors of the heart will seize the patient; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the wound with cauterizations and other treatments, as long as it is healing; and if it cannot heal, then know that there is a fistula; so treat it just as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut of sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse, or in the back, then treat it with what is before [it]; if it is large, sew it; and if it is small, powder it, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has broken pieces, cleanse the wound, and pull out any foreign bodies that are visible; and if there are none, let the wound rot, for this will facilitate extraction; and for other wounds on other members, make a judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a broken or ruptured uterus
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from the large wound the intestines sometimes burst out, or the membranes of the intestines, by which the introduction of them; and suturing it is more difficult, and sometimes worse than the small wound is bad, therefore one puts back the intestines in [them] only cold, if not put them in warm to warm; because the intestines inflate immediately when they feel the cold, so they go in better, and for this reason a medium-sized wound is worse, therefore one resets the intestine to its place rather than with others two. And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: the two common sutures occur in the suturing of the belly, and the suturing of other wounds of the body and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds; and nevertheless they are more suitable with the suturing of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines has escaped, and it seems easy to treat, it can be done in one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflamed from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or an old cloth in tepid water only, or boil in hot water with cypress and spikenard, and soak the intestine so that the swelling is gone; and once you have done this, restrain it from bleeding, and be careful that it does not burst to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with water or hot ale and mustard are cooked, for by this means the entrance is cleared of something; and if it cannot enter, make a small hole in the wound with the instrument with which we cut blood clots; and the first treatment is to cauterize the wound, that none of us should cut into it without great necessity; and this is the instrument to split it: cut inside along the curve and not outward, and look at this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have jumped out, so place them back again according to their natural form in their proper place, if you are able, for this will be useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is in the part under the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part under the belly, then put their head and chest higher than the parts below, and similarly arrange the wounded area so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to follow what I say for large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Make the patient put on the clothes that are provided to them, then take in your hands a linen cloth which covers all the wound and grasp its edges; and assemble the lips. And this is the common method of stitching, which is that you take one needle or more, according to the size of the wound's width, then leave about the head of the wound an inch of space, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce the two eyes of the skin with the two eyes of the siphac, which are under the skin inside, so that you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the two ends of the siphac together. Then take hold of a double thread around the needle of two parts, then assemble the two edges of the wound together properly, and then leave about an inch of space, and insert another needle; then tie the thread like you have done with the first needle, and do not stop doing this as often as you need needles until the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be moderate, between fine and coarse, because fine needles pierce all the flesh, and too coarse ones cannot well enter: therefore it is necessary that they are moderate. And it is not necessary to insert the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they open and cut the wound before the stitch; and then clip off the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and I place tents or cloths on the ends of the needles for usefulness to keep them, and leave them until the wound is sewn up. And this method of stitching with needles is more advisable in small wounds, because it suffices with one needle or two; the second stitch is common, which is that you assemble the two eyes of the skin and the two eyes of the siphac together onto a needle where there is strong moderate thread; and when you have pierced those four holes altogether, then take hold of the needle at the part where you started in the manner in which one sews clothes. And leave about an inch's worth of space between each stitch's width; this stitch is known to men, and I stitched a wound that was on a man's belly, who was wounded by a knife, and the wound was over a palm in size, and the intestines were well two palms in size, and the wound was on the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back to his intestines after he had been 24 hours empty, and the wound was sewn up just in 15 days, and I healed him, and he became whole.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judged that he was going to die, and it was a miracle; and I did not heal him with ointment, because I was in a place where there was none found, nor any medicine; and I put on more than twice a day cotton above the wound, and washed it with honey water until he became whole.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and push it from the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced the leather straight through, then let the head of the thread or suture where you have pushed in the needle and make it pierce on the other side from the inner part to the outer part; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as the tanner makes the furs, and that you leave once the thread on one side and take it up on the other, until the suture is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suturing, which the Greeks call properly, is such as some do who assemble the two parts naturally together and apply one end of the needle to the other end, in this way: insert a needle or end of the thread close by and make it pierce only that place, and leave the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outer part just up to the inner part through both ends of the thread; then make both pierce from the outer part just up to the inner part through two other holes in the thread which are on the other side; and this is the better manner of suturing and most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say this word, and some witness to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, or thread in each; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and know that when the rupture is inside the belly, then the suture is more difficult than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such that if you find the fresh wound with all its blood, just as the fire has changed it, then put back the intestines and the fat; then put on powdering charcoal dust, and if the fire has changed it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and thread the thread, and bind up the sinew and the tendon; then cure the wound just like the others, until it be healed; and if you don't have medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to start healing, old cotton, and move it 2 times a day until it be healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need another medicine in many simple situations where the wounds are plain; and if you doubt that the wound does not bring community to the principal members, then it is necessary that you soak light wool in tempered warm oil, or in rose oil, and put it around the shoulders, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or irritation in the bowels, and many times occurs, then cleanse them with black wine vinegar enema, and similarly if the irritation comes just to the intestine; and puncture inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are hurt, and this is because of the emptiness of their veins that are in them, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the approach of its nature to the nails.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the ligament jumps out of the wound, put it back again just like the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, you must tie back the part that is black, so that bleeding does not occur there, because veins and arteries are in it; then cut what is between the ligament, and let the two ends hang from the part under the wound up to the surface to lighten the extraction when the ligament falls, and the wound will close.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one can restore it in some people, because I have seen a man wounded with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became swollen and turned into an abscess, and there was discharge and flatulence coming from it; I applied treatment to it according to what I knew, and did not stop fine-tuning until he was healed, and the join mended.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him being sutured, I doubted that the patient would be ill in his stomach; and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experienced practitioners said that whenever he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take large flax threads, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the flax thread has opened the mouth, place it on the two lips, so that it tightens its mouth on; and then strike the head, and it stays so that he cannot untie it, then put another piece of flax after in this manner as before, until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That gut should be sewn in the intestine, and it does not come to any harm for the patient, and one can sew the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that is quite clean, and then tie at the head of this thread one thread of fine linen twine, then push the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and sew it up in the suture; and this way of sewing with flax is not different from the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the curved intestines, there is no remedy or cure, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of an ulcer or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is universally called a "fistula"; and indeed when it is filled with pus and flows downward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its verdant nodation, false and hard and white, or where you feel no pain, and it is also filled with pus like the feathers of a bird; and sometimes flows clear liquid downward, and sometimes thickened; sometimes little, and sometimes abundant; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is outside only due to one of the nine causes: namely, by the thinness of blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and above the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is corrupted, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in treatment; or because the corruption is a manner of plague; or because the property in the region is slow digestion, and late healing, and follows by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary that I inform you about the treatment for fistula made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the major veins and arteries and nerves or to the intestines or bladder or to some of the ribs or to the spine of the back or to any joint of the hands or feet; and thus to the principal part of the member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous sanitation, and there is no remedy but surgery, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come just to the place I said, and you have faith in its cure, and you see it well, then take a tent of tin or iron, if the fistula is straight, probe it; and if the fistula is twisted, search with a subtle probe made of cloth, for the cloth bends around the twistiness; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot probe it well with probes, purify it through one of the openings, for the moistness runs from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then cauterize the incision as your ability allows you, knowing whether there are bones or nerves, and is it deep inside, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when pressing with your hand, and where he feels it; and when you know truly where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the places I told you, then probe according to what I told you, and remove the false growths and corrupt flesh that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well-deeped in a straight place, it is necessary for you to probe deep, as long as you can, then put moistened probes of medicinal soap in them, and stick them just up to the head of the fistula, as long as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments made with healthy flesh, until they are healed; and if it is not healed by these means, then cauterize it, as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, probe it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.
