If the vein or artery does not bleed or severely wound the main member, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then wash it until the corruption is entirely removed, then treat with things that bring in fresh flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and becomes worse than before, know that you are not yet deep enough: uncover and clean until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore its place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	Know that if not, know that the corruption is too deep in and you cannot reach it; there's no other remedy than to let nature heal it; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with forceps, then take it out with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, then extract them all, do not leave one; and if moisture hinders you and there's no error or fear, scrape and clean the flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put a thing of caustic on the wound to rot it, and leave until the pus is all around the bones; and then they will be more easily separated; and if it is a large bone, such as that of the leg or thigh, repair only the corruption until the blackness is completely gone, then repair the wound; and if there is great part of the corrupted matter, and it comes just to the flesh of the bone; then you must remove and scrape all up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is sound; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from an internal cause, so that the matter came to the leg, and he had a large abscess, and there was no way to open it up; but the doctors worked on him so much that they opened the abscess, and they were draining out a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and there were many openings from which everything flowed, both blood and moisture from his body; and many physicians had treated him for 2 years, without any success in the art of healing, until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what was flowing through the openings all over his body; and his face became red, and it had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitch a tent in one of these holes, and then search all the holes, and find that one comes up against another from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and probed in one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it to be corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone inside; I cleaned out what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption than that which I removed; and I began to treat the wound with medicines over a long time, but could not heal it; then I started again, and found the bone as before, and discovered the corruption continued in the bone, and I cleaned it out, and then removed it, and bent myself to heal the place; but I couldn't do so until I probed around a palm's length of the bone, and pulled it back to its entire shape, then treated it with medicines; and it was healed and joined quickly, and there was no need to start again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the evacuation [of blood], it often bled profusely, but was completely cured, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and it was in good condition and had no harm or disadvantage from beginning to end, whether at coming or going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, you must treat it thusly: take a thread and hold it at the head of the bone that shows, and command someone to stretch it up; and take another linen string thicker than the first thread, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone, and be steady so that you draw out the corrupt flesh beneath, and uncover the healthy flesh on the place where you see how it should heal, so that it doesn't hurt the flesh; and put a dressing or a board under the bone to cover the corrupt flesh; and you must treat it until you can see and feel the corruption, and then treat it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open at all, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, uncover the flesh entirely; then put a stick underneath, and then pull with thread from one part to the other the corruption, and be the thread long enough according to the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut out the corrupted joint, and draw out the bone where it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy but to cut it; and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand or in the knuckle of the foot, that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must find out how that corrosion appears to you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or the nerve does not make it contrary; and know that the instrument for cutting these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance, and their grossness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare each one's instrument according to its resemblance of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument with which you will have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases; so think about the instrument with which you have need according to what it behooves.
dou feu	and from fire (to sterilize and purify).
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The flesh can be corrupted either from within or from without; and when you have medicined this corruption with the remedy of medicines, and it does not help, then it is necessary to cut that member down to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or by the greater evil, that is the failure of the member. And the signs are that the members become black, so that they seem burned by fire; and after the blackness, the corruption of the member spreads from member to member, and takes over all the body. If you delay in cutting, and this is due to the bite of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corruption is at the head of the thigh, then cut it off, and do not give him any space for coming up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, then cut at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no other remedy than to let the patient die with the quantity of their virtue; and do thus also when the corruption comes up to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, then cut after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, then cut the whole foot; and if it rises in the leg, then cut at the knee joint; and if it comes from above the knee, then there is no other remedy than to let the patient die from this affliction. And the manner of cutting or sooking the member is that you bind it up and down, and stretch a servant's cloak downwards and another servant's cloak upwards, and you loosen the flesh that is between the two cloaks by an inch wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or soak, and put a linen cloth on each side so that the soaking does not touch the healthy place, and come up to another lesion and swelling in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding comes from the wound when you operate, then cauterize the area quickly, or put some constricting powders on it; then come back to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I shall tell you what happened to a man in my town: he had a gangrene that seemed like a burning fire, and that corruption first came to his toe of the foot, so much so that it consumed the whole foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he quickly cauterized the foot, and was healed; and long afterwards the corruption came back to the same toe of the hand, and he came to me, and I put some reflective things on him after purifying his body, and the corruption could not cease; and he wished that I would amputate his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of reverting the matter; and also I feared that if I cut off his hand, that he would die, because the man's virtue was weak; and he entirely despaired, and came back to his land, and quickly cauterized his hand, and was healed; and I have only told this story for what others do in similar cases when they are necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess forms in the fatty part of the skin, and stays so long that it gathers a great deal of pus; and then it bursts and breaks through, and the pus flows out from the site, just like water from a vessel. And the skin on top is just as delicate as silk fabric, and does not spread until it reaches the bone or the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain", and it is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so long that it comes to the bone very close, then it is called "fistula". The treatment is that you scrape off all that skin around it, and even when it is delicate, just like silk fabric; and it does not need to be cut out for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you think the skin is scabbed over and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick from fat, then cure it with a suppository thus: look to see if the breast is large, and the tube that comes out of it has a foul odor, then make the Egyptian medicine as follows: take saffron, oil, and lapis lazuli, equally, and put it in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and thick like honey; and then take some of this according to your need and mix it with water and honey, and apply it as a suppository to the breast and close the opening; and let the medicine stay inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed and the pus is gone; sometimes a suppository made from ashwater is used when this medicine is not present, and that you take ashes of grapevine wood and pour water on them, then drain it and apply it as a suppository until you know the breast is well cleansed. And if the patient cannot suffer it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor ashwater, then use a suppository made with water and honey or there is one drop of lapis lazuli in it; or you make a suppository of honey and sweet wine which has the property to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the abscess scab over; and when you have done this and think the breast is well cleansed, then use a suppository that causes flesh to form there, and is made with powdered diaphanum and mixed with rose oil and wine; or you make a suppository of various medicines and ointments, of which I have said their properties in treating ointments; and if the opening of the abscess is small, and the tube of the suppository cannot enter it, then widen it with a piece of iron and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then cut around it and leave just enough space for the opening that the suppository can enter, and if the abscess that emits pus is above, then scrape it lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bow is in deep position, let no flesh be left to rot; and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see, prepare it so that the bow goes to its lowest point as it is, for when the bow is in deep position, let no flesh be left to rot and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see, prepare it thus: so that the bow runs lightly downward, and leave nothing of the bow; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and sit above the linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut at the strongest point the boil on the breast which is a little larger than the first, then apply ointment sweetly above the other cloth according to the size of the boil, and put it on the boil of the wound to ease the bow, and do not take away the large cloth outside that after many days once; and that which is on the boil of the breast, remove often to remove the bow, and know what comes out of the bow, if it's poison or pus or enough or digested or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has expanded in this manner and you see the nature that rises on the boil of the wound, then know that the breast is cured already, and approach health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the milk flows with undigested blood for many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come out after a long time, do not lose hope of health, for the patients approach health.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who recover slowly from scar tissue in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if indigestive bile shoots out of the heart after many days, know that the lungs have not healed; and if the lungs take long to heal, and are inflamed, mix dry medicines in substance and dry virtues, such as refined ointment, for it contains a great part of vinegar, and this is the last medicine; take refined ointment, and make it with rose oil, and equal parts of old wine; then melt it and use it; and do the same thing when honey thickened is present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is on the fire; then put the cloth in the broth, and place it on the heart, and sometimes administer a long aristolochic, and roots of celestial lily, which is also like flour of vetches and centaury; and use from simples or compounded ones: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption has gone deep, and has made a pressure in the bone, or in hard members, or in ligaments; so do the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil or pustule on the finger.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is a swelling that arises under the finger of the palm, or of the foot, or by chance in other parts; and when it becomes elderly, and one does not take care of it, so it comes to the great swelling, and runs and pours forth pus as long as the root of the boil runs, and by chance may run all over; and comes the corrosion just up to the bone, as long as it causes foul pain, and the finger joints are swollen, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not profit, then you must cut into it all the way through with a sharp knife, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the boil is healthy; and if the boil presses against the flesh, begins to prick and cut, then you must put hot oil under the boil that pricks the flesh, and let it rise up, and cut away the delicate and slight flesh, and apply on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out, and take away the flesh, for as long as the corrupted bone remains inside, it cannot heal; and if you see the vertebra corrupting, then cut into it there with an instrument as was said before, until it heals; and if it has become hard, and is pressing, and causes great pain, then you must first treat it; afterwards cut on the angle of the spittle-wood with a diagonal cut above, and beware that the cut does not reach all the way to the flesh which is under the angle, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, put something over it which soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the ear in the hand (i.e. a type of swelling or inflammation).
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The vertebrae that arise in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is a part where there are bones, and sometimes there is an angle, and one of them arises at the root of the joint, or the birthmark is on some of the vertebrae.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any notch of the two bones does not move, and he who is born at the jointure of the two bones may possibly move; the size of that one who is fatty is light, namely: measure it from its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that occur at the root of the joint are grievous to cure, and you should hesitate before cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that who is born or swells in the last notch, it is necessary that you cut around the flesh up to the bone first, then cut the bone with a string suitable for that, then dress it until it be healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that occurs on the fingers together comes from birth, or a boil, or scorching by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the suture, so that it may be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or moistened cloths in olive oil, so that they do not stick together; or put between two fine pieces of cloth, until the place be sewn up, as it should.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling occurs on any of his fingers with the palm, cut out that swelling in the way it is necessary.
des vils	of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are swollen, bulging, full of melancholic superfluities, which come upon many members of the body; and there are more in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to them occasional purging with vinegar, and then heal the boil with balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron cure is done in two ways: one where they cut them and let out the black blood; and the other way is that you tie the vein and let it bleed all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is done in this way: first raise the patient's leg with a hot iron very strongly, until the thick vein is thinned out; then tie the patient's leg from above the knee to the part below the kneecap; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three, with a wide knife; then lift and let out the black blood at your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood is let out as the patient can endure; and then tie it, and command him that he eat lean, cold meat; and recommence the evacuation and washing when the veins are full, and harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the wound is in this manner: bind up the patient's leg if it has a lot of hair, then put it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red and swollen; and if you don't have a bath, heat it at the fire, and then wrap a bandage around the vein on the long part of the thigh, or in the part below the knee; then loosen the skin to the vein, and scrape off the scab from each side until it seems as though one feels it; and it appears red and black, and when it goes into the skin it seems just like a white cord; then tie on the other end, so that it is loosened from the skin, and then wrap it with a light bandage, then wrap it in another place three days hence; then scrape off the scab on top of the vein until you see it, then lift it up as you have done, and wrap it with another bandage as you have done first; then cut off another strip, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut into the base of the foot, then pull out and lift just to the second strip; then take it from strip to strip until it is completely free, then cut it; and if you can't pull it out and lift it, then put a needle in all the thread very tightly double, and tie it and pull it, and put underneath the bandage, and turn your hand one way and another until it comes out; and beware that it doesn't cut, for if it cuts, then it cannot be pulled or lifted, and harm will come to the patient; and when you have pulled it all out, then put on the place of the wound moistened wool in vinegar and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the eye is contracted and twisted and wrinkled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it awry, but do not cover it up; and treat it in the manner which we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one covers the eye is curved, and does not pierce it, so that it may cover the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were subtle, it would pierce the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the thighs, in hot parts where no herbs or tree grow, and in dry land where there is little moisture; and it may also be found elsewhere than in the thighs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes from beneath the skin, as snakes and worms come forth inside the body between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this inflammation are such that it comes to the leg a great swelling; then the place changes and the inflammation begins to come out, just as a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the swelling appears, you must wrap around a piece of linen cloth about one and a half hands long up to II inches, and the node, and let the linen stay on the leg, and every time it points out at the front, rewrap the linen and the node; and if it is too long, cut off a part, wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it in its root until it comes out completely; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and make an abscess or putrefaction at the place, and a bad disease; on that account it must be treated bit by bit up to the head, and nothing remains inside the body; sometimes this swelling, when it is treated from V palms long, or from X, and one came to me, from whom it issued of X palms long, and when you cut it, it bursts into I or 2 sores, and it perforates right up to its bottom, so that everything comes out; and the material inside is emptied, and medicines are applied to the place every day to prevent putrefaction, then it cures just like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at any time on this vein are many veins, and just as much when it opens in the joint of the foot, or either foot, and there comes a lot of pus, and from which it runs rain; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "disease of oxen", for it has often afflicted cattle, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all through the body rising and falling, and it feels very well as it moves from limb to limb, until it bursts out of the skin where it goes, and causes a foul discharge; and it is believed to come from corruption of some humors, such as worms and serpents and lice and tapeworms in the belly; and one doubts its wickedness, for when it goes through the body and reaches the head, and gets into the eye, by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and drawn out, one cannot avoid that as long as it lasts: so then you must tie the place above and below with a strong tight cord; then cut up and draw it out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you don't find it, then cauterize with fire on top of it until it rots; and the greatest harm that it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or its head near the eye, then tightly bind underneath it a bandage, then cut up and draw it out; and the patient must be treated with purging of the body by soluble medicines for bad humors, and warn them to abstain from putrid foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from windness (or indigestion)
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and it can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to an ailing woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and later on, I saw it rise as well as a worm at the shoulder, just as quick as living silver when it runs from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and lodged itself in the shoulder, and then a little while after ran through the whole body, so that it came into the other arm; then she told me that she was constantly turning around the body, as I also saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it moved from member to member, because I had never seen this illness in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had always believed that the pain would move from one place to another, but I did not see it in the woman, and I thought that this was because the woman's body was dry, and her veins were hidden, and for this reason the aforementioned symptom appeared; and they do not occur according to this reason with those who are lubricous, and who have moist bodies and restored veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens like we have said, then bind tight above and below with a bandage; and then cut on top until the swelling is constricted back to its place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see to yourself, then cure it by using those who drive out the swellings, such as fetid pills and serpent pills and similar others.
des saiettes	from arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Splinters are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their heads is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and pointed ones, and blunt ones; and those with two angles, and those with shafts, and those with fragments; and the one that lodges in any member does so in one of two ways: either it penetrates a main member, such as brain, heart, liver, womb, veins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then into any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appears to you: so it behoves you to beware of the extraction of this arrow, for many die afterwards in various dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply imbedded, then draw it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the head when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the cerebellum leaps out which is above the brain, is when there are scotoma and sodor and convulsion and vertigo in them, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and commotion of understanding, and vomiting of gall; and perhaps it comes out through the nostrils or ears; and perhaps the speech and voice are lost; and there is a moist white discharge from the wound resembling a poultice, and also as black as charcoal; and if these signs appear to you, then keep away from the cure, and draw out the arrow unless it is in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of an arrow wound to the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and possibly the arrowhead moves like a hair, and there is dark blood, and cold sweat, and fainting: be certain then without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the splinter that never leaves the spleen is that a foam bursts out from the wound and the throat swells up, and the patient's skin turns color, and they gasp high and cry for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the splinter falls in the covering of the intestines, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great distress, and they gasp; and all the members from the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the splinter falls in the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat bursts out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow sticks in the stomach and jumps into the intestine through a hole, then there is no hope for treatment nor extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow sticks in the bladder and urine jumps out and comes out through it, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arm and neck and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and forearm and elbow and knee and toes and the limbs similar to them, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, therefore do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one man that an arrow shot into the eye socket in the root of the nose: I tested it and pulled it out from the other side under the ear fat, and he was healed without any hurt.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that had shot into the fat of the eye under the eyebrow skin, and the arrowhead was bent back, and I could only catch hold of the tip towards the bowstring, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow's string, all of one light iron without ears; the archer was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And draw out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arab arrow with ears; I pulled out the fletching, and refined it so much that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And draw out an arrow from his home that had been stuck in his belly, and I thought he was dying; and then it had passed 30 days, and he didn't change his condition; I cut into the arrow shaft, and shaped it, and drew it out, and there wasn't a bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who was shot in the back by an arrow, and the wound had healed on top; and the arrow remained inside him, and didn't change his natural disposition, nor did it cause him any harm in his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man, to whom an arrow shot into his face, and the wound had healed; and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And take an arrow from the king's son who it had fallen into his side, which was inclined to the left part; and the arrow was completely imbedded. I was called for the treatment after it had been stuck in him for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched it with a fine probe and did not find it; and he felt piercing and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I put a poultice of attracting and digesting things on top of it so that the area would not swell; and the location of the arrow became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the poultice on it for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient stayed that way a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his side; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied medicinal ointment with corrosive properties by hand daily until the wound was completely open; and I tested it, and felt the head of the arrowhead growing numb at its place; then I inserted into the opening of the wound that medicinal ointment, so long as the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and the terminal part did well for nearly four months, and then broke free in such a way that I stuck tongs into it on both sides, and it could not come out; then I ceased not to subtilize and engineer with various instruments, until I grasped it one day with tongs made well, according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, so long as I pulled it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise men judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was closed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you may place your care on what I do not say, for books cannot take up everything; but wise masters come upon great small things, and those present and defective, they find new work, and a new instrument, in the descent of strange things which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not protrude from the limbs where they are lodged except in two manners: either by the place where they enter, or by some other part; and those which exit through the place where they entered, are arrows entering fleshy places, and now sometimes shoot out.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not shoot now, leave it so that the flesh around is putrid and the issue becomes suppurated; and also if it is lodged in the bone and cannot exit, leave it thus for some days and move it each day; and then it will shoot out, and if it does not shoot out, make an incision all around with a very sharp instrument, so that the place around is widened, and then draw it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and among the accidents that I have mentioned it becomes apparent to the patient: do not pull it out, but let it remain for a few days until it grows equal again, because if the arrow comes close to the skull, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself and does not come close to the skull, and the patient remains for a few days without bad accidents, then one should think about pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply stuck and cannot come out, administer tarers around it, as I have told you; then care for the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is reset in its place in the body and it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the tent. And if you feel it, then pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then wait until the wound becomes larger; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to which it holds, remove the flesh that is stuck in it from two parts as far as you can, and then break or bend the arrow's ears so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you would pull it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out once, leave it until the surrounding flesh is corrupted, then pull it out, for the extraction will be made clear.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding does contrary to what we have said of its treatment in this chapter; and be careful of incision into the nerve and vein, and know how you can draw out the arrow without danger, soon or late, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow hit him, for that is the greatest aid, and if you cannot, so do it according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another place, or if it has pierced any part of him, or the skin is swollen in the place where you see or feel it apparently: then cut above, so long as the tongs can take hold, and then pull it out: if it jumps forth now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand around gently, so that it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, so leave it for now, and then start the extraction again until it comes forth; and if the shaft of the arrow is inside him, then push in all of the shaft; and if the shaft has splintered, and you wish to administer poultice, administer the instrument beveled, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push it out, and if the arrow is embedded, then insert the instrument with a pointed tip inside him, in order to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all of the flesh around where the poison is, if possible; then heal the wound as it is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls in or on the back or belly or bladder or ribcage and is nearby and you can cut on it, cut into it; be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and then sew up the wound if necessary; and cure it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs used to pull out arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, small, and tiny, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrow's fletching is also like the feathers of a bird, to guide it at the point of the arrow, as in this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and knowing if it fits thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	arteries of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins by which one recovers are XXXI, of which there are XVI on the head, to wit: two beats that are after the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in two temples visible; and two veins that are in the corners of the two eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is on the crown of the head; and the two gullets that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the upper lip, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins whose cuts are commonly used are the V shape in each arm: one is called "the vein of the head" and it is located on the left side; and the second is called "the cut" and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call the common people "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and they call the common people "vein of the belly", and it is above the elbow, and it is that one whose cut shows itself openly on the arm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the Salvador vein is the one that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the fold of the pocket on the left side, and the second Sophene which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse" which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears so helps the ancient cathartics and migraine; and the qualities of the bloodletter, as I say to you, are that you raise the patient's head, and scrub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tie the patient's neck with a cord until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head: when they do, take hold of them and draw it up; then take the lancet, and push it under the vein just to the bone, then lift your hand all the way along the vein downwards, and cut and the skin and the vein well with two cuts of the traverser, and make blood come out until you see it; then tie it off and fasten it, so that it is healed; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth an old remedy, and a habit for sore eyes, and a custom for sharp pains at the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is such as I say: it is when the patient strains his neck, so that the two veins appear clearly; and feels the lump under his thumb, then signs to have it done; then lift the key above the vein up to your thumb index, and insert the lancet underneath, and raise the vein up and cut it, as you did in the other two veins, and make a thread of blood according to your necessity; then unbind the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then bind it firmly, and let it stay until it is healed; and we have spoken about its clotting and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for ancient face diseases, and for migraine, and for scurviness; and the quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, so that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Put the point over the vein and hold it with your hand or something else, and let two bloods come out according to the quantity that you see; then tie the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is sewn and once the work has been done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not suitable that the burns be too severe, and the bleeding cross over, because the bone is close by, and it's possible that the burn will break through when it becomes more subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting from the two veins that are in the arm is helpful for the eyes, and for the itch, and for the redness, and for the oreiule in the eye, and for facial diseases; and the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient tightens his neck by twisting with some string, just as before; then let it bleed, and let the blood be dark, a little long of the flame a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the burn becomes subtle, it may break through; then let out blood as much as you need, and then bind up with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bloodletting from the vein of the neck is worth for ague and for severe fever, and for facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his neck to your left hand, and takes a thin flame long, and puts it between the two nostrils in the space, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start to flow now; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your necessity, then tie it one night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.
