The salve of two gum arabic's does help in the tightening of the ligaments, and in the beginning of surgery, and in many diseases, and in swelling, and in corrosion, and in herpes, and boils; and the quality of the salve is that the patient ties a cord around his neck with one end under one arm and the other under the other, as we have said; and let the master be on top of the chief part of the sick person, and the sick person tie himself onto the seat, then make an incision in the vein of the long one somewhat wide, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is needed; then make another cut in the other vein, then untie the string, and hold both veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and let him leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the salve of books (note: this seems to be a phrase or term being used in this text)
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins on the upper lips is said to help against sores in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and around the neck.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the treatment is to have the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at both veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black spots: cut both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest from each side, and do the same for the two veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the treatment under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The treatment of the veins under the tongue is helpful after the treatment of the cephalic vein, and it's for the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and mouth diseases; and the quality of the surgeon is that the patient will spit between your hands in front of the sun, and lift up their tongue, and look under each side a black vein: cut then both, and do not go too deep because under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	Veins of great depth from which one commonly draws blood are healed in two ways: either they prick to the entire length of a flame-colored, wide mirtin or olive-like subtle cut as surgeons make, and is called "anesil"; and it is wide and subtle according to the wideness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is very well known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the hairy veins filled with thick and obvious blood, and that contain thick and turbid blood; and this is the shape of the flame-colored olive.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is finer when pointed, and is for healing fine veins, or where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed him carefully, and to spare the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and bleeding from blood comes, then it is necessary to stop it, as I said; and it should not be pricking with a flame, but cutting in such a way as for anasil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, you must draw it out and change another one; or you want some rain from it, or sew up the vein in the arm with thread: it opens clearly; and close the incision with fire, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the vein, you should then draw out the arm, that you touch the place until you recognize the pulse; then mark the place with ink and then tie up the arm, and close the vein with fire and ashes; and beware that you do not prick in the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is of the artery: be aware.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it come out as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery: hurry then and put your finger on it for a long time, then take your finger away when the bleeding stops, which often happens; tie up the arm and leave it thus, and do not move the patient's limb; and be careful, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it bothers you, and the medicine is not present, then strike the artery if it opens, because its head recedes; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a rind of fig tree, and make it, and take one half and bind it well up to the other joint; if the bleeding stops, that is well; if not, cure with the powder which stops blood; and the stoppering is not grievous in most dispositions for the small space of the wound, and the tightness of the bandage on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in a hollow is very useful which treats blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the surgeon should be careful for the nerve that is below, and if he pierces too deep and finds the nerve, it swells and the bleeding will be grievous, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often opens up and in some men because of its subtlety, you must remove the sutures from the instrument; and protect the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there are veins between the two nerves, then cut them long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding from the cephalic vein helps so much that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and you must bleed using a flaming olive or a flaming myrtle oil, because this is the safest of all the veins, because there are no nerves or arteries under it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In any case, you must seek the most convenient position and do nothing if it fails the first time, and try again; and by chance the place swells in some men when it fails the first time, but it does not cause harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of healing is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it is not done except to preserve health and to ward off future illnesses; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and you should bleed at the beginning of spring, summer, or autumn after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and you should bleed on either the first day or the third day, two to three hours after noon.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The medic who is ministered to the sick does not have a set time determined, but whenever there is need of day or night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not necessary to heal children up to 14 years, nor women carrying fruit until 7 months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should old people who have passed 60 years be healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some want to be healed, in whatever manner it is, it is necessary that he be told to empty his intestines with a light clyster, if he has much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not attract superfluous things harmful to the main members; and it does not heal him who is too full of meat, nor one who is drunk until he becomes sober, nor one who is dropsy-ed; and be careful not to heal after a passion of colic, vomiting, and evacuation of the belly, and frequenting with women, and labor, night-watching, and cohabiting, and all that belongs to virtue, or by something from arms or from body; then subtlety the humors, if the swelling is great, by meat and drink and medicine, if you are able; then go into a bath, if nothing prevents, to subtlety the blood, and heal him of the wound around the third part, as we have said; and keep that day from labor, pain, and lust, and similar things; and be joyful and happy, and let the healer be higher than he whom one heals, and wipe his arm two or three times, then tie the string above slowly, for if it is too tight or too loose, so the swelling cannot heal; and then wipe him with the hands until the veins swell, and can be felt; then moisten the healer's hand with a flame of old oil, then put his thumb from his left hand on that wound below the shoulder where he wants to heal, so the wound does not break out and fail to cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that flow like strings to the surgeon, and there are such that are full of windiness, so that when fire is placed on them, they retreat from the fire, and cannot be opened; and it is thus with us; and if the vein is avulsed, the wound is too narrow, therefore it behooves the surgeons to be knowledgeable in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the swelling bursts open the first time, it's good; but if not, then he should repeat it again a little below or above that same spot quickly, unless the place is still swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is inflamed, and the patient fears, let him leave it a day or two, and not bind the arm: perchance there will come inflamed abscesses; do not enter the bath, then start the treatment again if it pleases you; and if the opening is small, or the vein runs thinly, you doubt that it will not bleed as much as you see, so apply fire directly to this very opening itself; and make a poultice quickly, while the swelling is inflamed; for this has happened many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swelling increase, do not restart the bloodletting, and put a little drop of linseed oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and is moist in this place the line that the oil makes; and thus administer the linseed oil in every incision that you bleed the veins to stop the flow of blood; and do the same with treacle and poppy juice, when you put them on the swelling; so subtly does it clean out and separate what is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which has occurred many times, especially when it is not thoroughly bloodletted at that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hasten and put on the place a wet sponge in water and oil, hot, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has come out of the vein, and if any blackness or greenness remains at the place after some days, it does not harm him; and if you see, put on something made from aloes or myrrh dissolved in calamine juice, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there comes an abscess and appearance of illness at the site of the healing from the basilica: therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be cautious not to put on anything from what we have said, for perhaps the blood will flow from an artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the place, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each type of blood according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Since the joint is black, let it come out until it is red; and if you see a vein large, let it go until it becomes fine; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the thin and feeble person, and who needs bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and have the incision wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and he should be healed slowly and often, and one must heal him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this way of healing is safe from bleeding and numbing of the nerve, and it is more valuable than long or wide healing.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body is weakened by the bloodletting, it is necessary to give him moist bread in apple juice; if he is overheated, then drink 3 or 4 times the amount of blood; and if he has a cold complexion, then mix moist bread with sweetened syrup, or honeyed aromatic syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it spouts to the vein, after the issuance of much blood, it is necessary that it inhale broth of meat, and a sweet-smelling syrup, and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to evacuate his arm and heal another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great surgery, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue, continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to evacuate his arm after the first surgery, and he has a strong body, should heal in 7 hours after the first surgery, or after the 9th hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be healed from another side, should be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has much blood within the body which is already heated up and brings on fever; thus it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and to enlarge the cut so that it bursts in a pustule; then you must observe all the signs of vein-cutting, and place your hand over the pulse when it bleeds, lest death come instead of a pustule, and this happens many times when the surgeon is careless. And it is not necessary when you see the arm loosened, and blood issues again the second time, and the cut is closed, that you press hard on it; nor if it is crooked, that you stretch out the arm at once, for that would be bad; but leave it alone until it bleeds a second time. Or you point to the tip of the flame, as long as the congealed blood issues forth from the cut of the vein, and place on it a poultice made with thread soaked in water, and press down lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, let it be alone and do not bind it tight until the inflammation has calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to let blood again the second time, then heal it in the same place, or in another wound, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The wound on the arm is healed in that place instead of the wound of the head because it is complicated.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the cure is that the patient puts his hand into hot water until the flesh is red; then it should be tied moderately so that the vein appears well; and then let out the blood now through the needle, not too wide or long; and the holes should be large, and the blood should be let out very close to the joint of the hand; and if no more blood can come out, then put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood congeal in the water until you have enough; and if it is winter, do not put the hand in hot water again, because it is set in cold weather even more; and the cure of this vein is safer than all other veins, with no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cure of the vein in the right hand's wrist is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and put it into hot water until the vein is emptied, if you see it; and if the bleeding happens on its side, and you close the hole completely, nothing will harm; and do not go too deep in depth, because the nerves are beneath all the flesh exposed, and then put the hand in hot water again, if the blood has congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as it's necessary for you to let, then put on the swelling oil and bandage to bind quickly, and thus do with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The swelling on the left hand is worth the sickness of the gout, and do with it just as I told you to do with the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sores of the sophene are worth for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the loins, and retention of flower (perhaps "flowers" referring to blood vessels?), and disease of the kidneys, and hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its sore is that the patient puts their foot in hot water and rubs it on the ankle so long as it cracks, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and over the foot there go many veins; cure then the largest vein or at the ankle which moves first.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have taken out the swelling on top of the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and let it heal in the same way as when it is cut; and let the flesh become again normal.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood can't come out, then put the foot back in the water and let it bleed well out of the swelling.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the sores fail at first time, then repeat the second on top of a poultice, because the place is salty; do not doubt nerves, as we have said, and thus treat the sore of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic swelling is at the knee of the back leg, and its abscess is worth the pain in the back when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his blood is such that the patient goes into the bath, and rubs above the ankle four days in twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then let him bleed in all manner that you can, and crossing over; and be wary that you do not cut too much, for the place is sore, and it has been replied to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then bleed any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and near the little toe, and be wary of the nerves; and make so much bleeding as you see, and then release the bandage, and put on cotton and bind it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	venous bleedings by suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and bloodletting is done in two ways: either by piercing to attract blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this venous bleeding by suction is done in two manners: either it is on fire at all times, or not; and the venous bleeding which is made by cutting and extracting blood is made in 14 places of the body, where one is entirely under the head; and another under the neck; and two others in both sides of the neck; and a venous bleeding under the chin; and a venous bleeding on both shoulders; and a venous bleeding over the kidneys; and a venous bleeding in both arms; and a venous bleeding in both legs; and a venous bleeding in both ankles; and the venous bleeding does not treat with blood, unless for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it has not weakened anyone, just like making a venous bleeding of a vein; and it is not necessary to administer it, nor at all times nor not at all, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to necessity of illness it is necessary to bleed, or for custom, then we lead them outside each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at each time; for there are such who, when they have need to bleed, so have a heavy head; and such who find repletion and redness on their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes; and such who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and flow with blood; and there are such who sleep, and see through their own blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed when it is in the middle of the month, let us command that they be bled after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding from the nose so helps in treating the sickness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary for this to be after the evacuation of all the body; and this bleeding is a substitute for the bleeding of the brain, and it is not necessary for those who are of cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, for it does them much harm; and therefore it is not necessary for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed themselves, become forgetful, and for this reason the cupping glass should be placed a little lower on account of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The swelling below the neck is situated between the sinew of the head and the armpit. It is worth noting it at the constriction of the belly, and at the division of the channel of the womb, and at the throat, and at the fullness; and one must often press upon it, because if it holds too tightly, it obstructs respiration or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The swellings on both sides of the neck are worth noting as pains in the head, and obtalmie, and emigrainne, and at strangulation, and at pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is situated between the sinew of the armpit; and you must command the surgeon that he stretches his hand to put [something] in place so that he does not touch the artery, nor remove excessive blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The bloodlettings under the chin are worth for illnesses of the mouth, and for corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of bleeding from both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The bloodlettings on the shoulders are worth for illnesses that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The swellings of the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm because they draw blood from these thick veins; and command the surgeon that he not cut too deep there, for the place is bare of flesh and lies under nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is above the backside is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases below, and it's necessary that the cupping glass be large, and made of iron, so that it can draw well; and if it were subtle, it would break, and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs are quite effective, because they draw blood from all over the body, and are worth for old pains in the groin, and in the loins, and in the bladder, and help to dissipate the swelling; and they take the place of two saphena veins, and two ankles, but however, they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the cupping glass is that you first put it empty, and then suck immediately, and place it hastily, and move equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the blood appears redder; then remove, and put the cupping glasses back, and take care of the condition of the body, because there are some who have thick flesh, and clear pores: so it's necessary to hit only once, and it's necessary to make large cuts, and a little deep ones, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it's necessary to hit twice: the first time to thin the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the sinew is very thick, then you must strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out some blood little by little, it suffices to do this once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood to be shed, so that it is released often; and if the vein is thick, then pierce deep into it, and the ends should be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for one with hard skin and tough, and who have prominent pores, that you anoint the places of the venuesses with dissolving oil: as long as it is in summer, with violet oil, or oil of sweet almonds, or oil of melon seeds; and if it is in winter, with oil of cress, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or of balm, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person who is being treated has tender skin and large pores, then there should be no oil put on it, but rather it should be washed after venesection with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or melon seed water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, should rise with ass's milk, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive growths should take a lift of old wine, or vinegar of the same, or a decoction of yarrow or camomile, or similar things; and they do not need to be healed with a poultice before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they must not sleep after the poulticing, and it is necessary that they warm themselves up when they should be pouluced and are being poulucated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And take care of those who are being healed and have hot blood, and whose blood is too sharp and inflamed; it is necessary that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in the water, and similar things; and drink pomegranate juice, and roast kid meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, they should take honey syrup, and sweet-smelling wine that is between old and new, and drink pomegranate juice, and drink kid meat juice, and drink little birds and pigeons' juices; and the day when he will be poulticed, it is necessary for him to drink more than eat; and it is fitting to give some men sometimes treacle or muscatel before the poulticing, or after, in order to comfort the principal limbs; and be subtle with the blood, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Those that are put to strike are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the side and the flanks and the hip; for those members do not suffer being struck upon them, and one does this only in order to attract blood from member to member, as we put on the breast when the new moon bleeds; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put on ventouses on the belly and on the side to reduce the member; and it removes the pain, when there is an ulceration or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue by chance the ulceration, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus does it do it when one puts it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained humidity; and these ventouses are administered empty so that they suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot vinegar, as in the disease of the pleurisy, and in such a manner how one fills the ventouse with warm water only, or with water where it has been cooked herbs convenient to these.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the plaster administered on fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two palms wide and half a palm deep, and on the edge around the middle one small perforation, so as to insert a needle, and it should be of brass, soft in front so that it does not hurt the patient when putting it on the member; and there should be in the middle a bar of crossing brass or iron, to put a lamp enclosed, and there should be great and small ones according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the ventouses of children are different from the old, and the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And it should thus be put this ventouse above the member: take the lamp of wax or ointment, and put it inside the ventouse in the middle of the bar which is inside the ventouse, so that the light will be at the bottom of the ventouse so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the member, and the opening should be above the perforation which we have said, so that when you want to, if there is vapor, go away and take off the ventouse; and take again the ointment as before, and repeat often, if you need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass therefore which is administered in the disease of pleurisy, at all heat, has no rod nor hole, and is not administered except when it is full of water, and is placed on the member only; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cures are not administered except in members where one cannot put cups for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places denuded of flesh, such as the throat or neck, and others similar; and the quality of the patient is that when you find cures that are in sweet clean waters with a pleasant odor, take them; and put one in a sweet water, until they become accustomed, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let it be cleansed by vein and cupping, then rub the member as hard as it becomes red, and put on the cures; and when they are full, and swell, if it is a place where one can put a cup, then apply it, for this is worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the place of ease with a cloth, and then with water, very well, and then bind it; and if the wound heals too slowly around the body of the abscess, then moisten the linen cloth in cold water and put it on until the abscess is congealed; and if the abscess is multiplied, then put vitriol paste or glue, or similar things, on it until it cools down; or you place half of peeled chickpeas on the wound and leave them until they dry out to the wound, so that it will now congeal; and if you need more, take other abscesses.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the abscesses do not want to dry up, then rub the place of fresh blood on it, or you stick a needle in it until the pus comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they are bleeding, then sprinkle some aloes powder and charcoal dust, or soot, on top, and they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of wounds (or "The Book of Bruises").
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for wounds and swellings.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know this, dear son, that the foolish physician throws himself at this chapter, which never saw any of the old books nor letters; and because of this cause is strange the science in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except by the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described here in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments which are made, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So then it is fitting that we say the prologue of this book, which are the summaries of words and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been proven wise may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to treat the sick person on both sides, if any thing does not hinder it, as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if the time is very cold, or too hot; and a cold cholera, I mean cold jugs, meat of bird and goat, and do not drink wine, nor consume any greasy meats, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of warm abscess or spreading of matter in the member; if the patient returns to their former government which they used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make thick nourishment, or have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and eggs, and peas, and veal, and oysters, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the flesh is repaired more quickly and the wound heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well reattached or soldered according to their nature because of the looseness of the members, nor those also who are too soft, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, mend over the broken bone with large splints which have been hardened and joint the member together, until it is strengthened so that it was before; and do not remove him from his work, and for this reason he must be nourished with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that wounds are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the wound of the head is one thing, and the wound of the back or leg is another, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of wounds.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are wounds that go around an arm or leg, and others that cut into it, such as the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And also wounds with an open gash, and wounds with a small slit or tear.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each manner of treatment have its instrument and proper tool in the restoration, according to what the memory brings back into its place; and it is known that the fracture of the bone by what the location is twisted, and opens well on the outside, and sounds with pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break; but it may well have a twist, or split, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So do not move the hand, but put on medicines that come later, and then bind it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the breakage that goes in a circle, and are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary to put them back into place equally, thus as abscesses grow hot will come; and if abscesses hot come, then leave alone for a day, until the abscess be appeased; then put him back in place at an angle that you can easily and skillfully, and know that the restoration of it is more easy than the restorations of that which has pieces; then hold it, so as it needs to be afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is stretched by two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or to your hand it is a small limb, or to both cords, or to one cord and to your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you reattach by all means the additions in their places at an angle that you can, and take care that through your work there does not come to the patient injury or pain; and join well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels well to the touch if you think it is not quite right: straighten it well, and do not bind it too tightly, or press it as those who bring heat and constriction to the member by their work, as we have said many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, instruct the patient to stay still so it doesn't move, neither while awake nor asleep, neither turning over nor otherwise; and be sure that the limb is secure so he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and you must put him in such a condition that he feels no pain; and watch that it is set straight, lest there be tortuousness when it is reset; and the quality of the broken limb will be according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as hands and feet and similar: it is necessary to envelop them in a soft and subtle cloth of linen; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to envelop them in a wide and strong strip of linen, because the broad strips encircle the entire great limb and hold it tight from all parts equally, so there is no slackness; then tie around light pads, three turns or four according to the limb, and grasp with one hand a piece of cloth at the entire strip, then go above the break and hold it less tightly, that the break may be a little apart from the break; and soften the cloth a little by little, as much as you take a good part of the healthy place, then take the other strip, and turn around again down on the broken limb; then go back to the part below the break, and hold it moderately, not too strongly nor too gently, as we have said in the first instruction above; then put between the strips pads of linen or cloth, so that they are all equal, then tie everything over with a bandage, and then put your well-made straps on, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put something soothing on the abscess that is hot, and which draws out the swelling, and leave it thus for some days; then bind upon the eyes with stars, and be of half of a wide piece of linen sewn up, or of wood from which one makes nails, or of palm splints, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the star that one puts on the break is a little thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as it is necessary for the member of small or great size; then bind upon the stars just as you have done at the first layer, then tie above a cord appropriately, just as in the first layer on the break; tighter up, the less; and it must be that the cord are middle-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and be of fine linen; for if the cord are thick, like I have seen the works of fools who make their bandages of twisted linen cords, and that is a great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and must not have between each star less than two fingers' breadth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the splints' ends after being bound in their healthy places, then put under them linen wrappings or torn flannel, so that they do not become worse.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the skin is torn, I will tell you the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not need to bind with splints all broken members at first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Car when the members are great, there is no need to apply cauterization stronger than a seventh of a day or seven days, or more according to your safety regarding hot swelling; and see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting: and that you take from the flour that remains at the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundance of egg, and put this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster restoring breakage to many dispositions, and even for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of ointment that restores breaks, dislocations, and twists: take 3 parts of alum, laudanum, and galena, and gum arabic and myrrh, ana 20 parts; myrrh and aloes, ana 5 parts; and aloe, 9 parts. And make them into powder, and mix with abundance of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this ointment, because it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other manner of plaster that is good for twisting: take myrrh and vervain, nine parts; galbanum and aloes, eight parts; aloe six parts; Armenian balm ten parts, and grind well, and mix with vinegar or abundance of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to plaster joints and bones dislocated from their places, and to calm the pain occurring, and to dress the crack in the bone: take new linen, and soak it in ash and boiled oil, and place it on the spot.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not cure [it], but they are good for calming a hot abscess, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of ointment that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and wild ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the repair of a crack in the bone and to reduce the remaining part of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of valerian, camomile, flowers of violets, meal of vinegar, of each one part; and crush, and mix with wine, and warm the member, then mix it with moisted water of coriander or of water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of applying ointment more strongly than the first, when a hardened abscess comes to restoring the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and marjoram, and flowers of violets and chamomile, in equal parts; and grind them, and cook with vinegar of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates says that for the restoration of a broken member, one should only use a wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that for the restoration of a broken member, one should put on things which are slightly hot and dry, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of ointment that is worth for lesion and pain: take myrrh and crushed horn of a wild goat, or bird's quill, and vellum, in equal parts, and grind them, and make an ointment with it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen the bandage after a little while, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved out of its place; if it does not loosen for several days. And if there is pain at the point, or itching, without rest or swelling, if it comes to a head, hurry and loosen it, and remove the ointment now; and take light cloth and a moist sea sponge, and dip in water, and lift up the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, dampened in water or rosie oil, and bind it with a nut, as long as you are sure of hot abscess; and let the inflammation of the member subside, and the pain be gone, then resume the gentle binding, and a little ointment, and do not strain it so hard as before; and continue thus until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the swelling is gone, and redness and pain and inflammation have ceased entirely, and you need to apply a poultice and binding again, so do it again, as you did first treatment.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the member of what we have said, do not loosen until after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7; and sometimes let it be for 20 days, according to what one sees, as long as the inflammation subsides, and approaches the skin above; then tighten the bandage more than before, and thicken its flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the area is drying too much out of necessity, know that suppurations cannot come; therefore loosen with hot water, every third day, and wash it once an hour; by this work, therefore, cut short the suppurations to the member, and quickly repair what foolish practitioners left twisted: this is bad, and it is a fearful operation, and I see nothing else but to let go and operate correctly.

Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of breaking, and various forms, and the causes are designated; for there are breaks that are made by striking with a sword, and the arm shatters all the bone down to the sillon which is under the bone, as does an axe or club; and therefore this manner of breaking is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above without piercing it, and is called this manner of bruising "absolute"; and the wound of these two bruises is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, or a fissure, or a bruise from a stone, or falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a bruise pressing, which approaches just to the skin that is under the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.
