And if there is a wound that has healed into the bone as finely as a hair split, and the crack is small, and therefore this break is called "capillary"; and if the wound which was made either by piercing with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and causes the piece of bone to go inside, and makes a hole that splits like when blacksmiths heat up the cauldrons, so the iron goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in skulls that have soft bones, such as the head of an infant; and it happens to all these ways of breaking where small pieces are pulled apart like this; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of bruises by the swelling on them, and the inflammation that has been tested, and by the corrupt flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary bruise is known by this: when the bone is uncovered and you rub your finger on it, if the bruise opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the bruise, be careful about the accidents that have befallen the patient. And if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of blood, loss of understanding, extension, palpitation, high fever, and the eyes coming out and becoming red, and other similar signs in more serious dispositions, then it cannot be healed with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it's in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone before the 14th day of the moon that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, so that the flesh under the bone is not corrupted, and the accidents which we have spoken of come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone comes just up to the cloth that covers the brain, you must cut into the broken part thus: and take hold of the patient's head injured, and uncover above the bone in every way that you can, and on the figure of the wound more gently than you can, and when the bleeding from decorum comes to reveal the bone, or abscess is hot, then help with what is necessary, and be sure of the cessation of bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut at the narrow trimming before, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I insert a second swelling, one greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have several different swellings, some thick and others wide, and are pointed, and of iron hardness; and work on them lightly, lest you lacerate the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and strong, it should be pierced around it, so that you can apply swellings with awls, but not so deep as for them to penetrate through the bone of the skull; and there should be above the point a border or a circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you need to have several of these, each coming into its place on the edge of the bone, so that you will have awls for all sides; and this is the shape of the three manners of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one awl on the bone, and turn it back and forth with your hands until you know the bone has been pierced; then put the awl in another place a little later, and do all around like this, and cut with the pincers the space of the bone which is between the piercings, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone to your hand, or with any of the tools you have such as tongs, forceps; and be sure not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perforated and treated the bone, you must take out the roughness that remains from the bone with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be more sharp and subtle than the other incisor; and if there is anything of the small bones or no scales left, then scrape them off lightly with instruments; then cure the wound with stitches and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of working is what Galen says, which is more safe; and he affirms it very strongly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, in the place where the break shows clearly; so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place beneath the head of this incisional lens the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sharp in two directions, so that the incision is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet upwards, so that you carefully chip all around the bone, and be careful of the membrane that is underneath; if it is attached to the bone, so scrape lightly, for one scrapes well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce all the way to the tissue, and the bone is chiseled only so far that it leaves small pieces, then you should cover over that roughness and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you should have in various quantities, in order to smooth out each part as well as possible, according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you go before large rasps and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate cuts and subtle breaks, you should smooth them out according to their direction. And it is a thing that cannot be easily mastered by one who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the pustule is uncovered, then you must take one linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and wet it with rose oil, and put it over the wound; then take another linen cloth doubled in two or three, and wet it with wine and rose oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this as lightly as possible so that you do not harm the pustule, then administer over the other strip some medicament, and do not pull on it too tightly until it just covers the wound; and let it be thus for one day or two, until the abscess has ceased to swell, then take it off, and apply medicines such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and frankincense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and apply medicaments gradually without scratching; and be careful that the wound is completely clean before you leave the ointment, or before you sew up the skin; for when the skin sews itself over the tissue under the brain, it corrupts and festers, and causes great evil to the patient; for when something biting is put on the pustule, it becomes infected above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any evil accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no pus coming out from it, unless it be due to the medicine that has been put on it, which has such virtue, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix one draught with it, and apply it to the swelling; then treat it in the manner of cures that is required, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that never are the two bones of the nose broken at once, or one by itself alone, for they are two separate bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it becomes dislocated or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should take your little finger or a perforated needle and put the equal length of that break inside your index finger and on the opposite side, until the bone returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and you cannot reach it with your little finger, then you should put it back into place with a wooden mallet, not too big.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then do it in the same way, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has cooled down, then bind a cloth of linen over the head of the bone, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you should place another cloth on the other part, if the break is there; and let the tents be so big that they fill the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some physician said that one must moisten the tents with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It doesn't seem right to me that it be done, but they must be moistened in the making of almond milk with egg and miller's powder; then let the tent stay, as long as the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at no time should you place an egg poultice in the nose instead of a tent, and if you have a soft cloth available, wrap it around and keep the breakage together, and breathe through the patient's nose. Do what seems best to you.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, put cerote or moistened cotton in rose oil or a small pouch of diachylon into the nostril.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses do not come out, so he puts a plaster on the outside with barley flour and incense powder, mixed with almond milk of egg, then puts lightest torches upon it, and binds him no tight; and if the break of the elbow is small, and it is broken into little pieces, so he extracts it by suitable tools for such, then sews the cut, and cures things that come out as charred flesh, and soldering, as with plasters and ointments suitable for such; and if there is no wound within the elbow, so he cures it with tents, and puts poultices on it, until they are healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet !
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is out of place, and there is no wound above it, and the fracture is so slight that only, and not at all broken in two, forward than bent inward, then one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left side of the mandible, then put your index finger from the right hand and push the fracture inward lightly, and fasten it to the other hand by outward, and make sure.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is split into two, it is necessary that you provide an extension of 2 inches by 3 inches until it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the dislodging of the teeth has happened, or bruising, then stretch threads from gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken mandible ointment, and put on one double cloth; and on the cloth a well-made great bandage, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and tie it up at your discretion that you can, and command the patient to rest, and give them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the patient's condition is changing, then unbind on the third day, and then reapply what has been changed; and put plaster on it, of mill powder with abundant egg or flaxseed flour, after having removed the ointment; and put on a light linen bandage. If the plaster hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as is until they are healed; many times people heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a boil or abscess appears, apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, remove the loose bone fragment from it; use subtle tools suitable for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, sew up the wound if it is large, and put on one suitable ointment to prevent scarring, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The shoulder blade breaks more than once in front of the shoulder, and the break is in three manners: either it is broken and separated into two pieces, and there are fragments, and this is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is such that when the break is without a wound, you have two assistants, one to hold the shoulder blade which is broken; and the other extend the neck towards the part; then place the break in your arms, so that the form be as it should be, and there is no appearance or bending.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded rod of cloth or linen, and make it as large as needed; then stretch and lift the shoulder blade, and hold the rod in your hand, so that you can put the break back into its proper place.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder blade out to the front because it is too deep, it is necessary that the patient lies on their back and places a middle bolster under their shoulder; then push the assistant down on the shoulder so that the bone of the shoulder blade is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your arms, and if you find it disjointed, it is necessary that you split it open; and pull out the fragments lightly, and if the bone cannot join together with any adjustment, cut it at one of the incisors that you have; but make sure to place this instrument under the shoulder blade so as to hold it in its proper position.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It seems like a cuillier and is not shaved, and is also as wide as it needs to be according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and has two heads, just as you see, and one head is wide and the other is narrow, just as is the laceration of the wound that you have made when you split the bones; and once you are sure of hot aposteme, the cut closes over the wound, and if the laceration is small or you doubt hot aposteme, then cover the wound with linen and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the hot inflammation comes, you should soak a piece of linen in rose oil, garlic, and wine, and apply it to the wound.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, is that you put on the bone a pouder dou molin and aubun d'uef plaster, and set lightest bandages on top, and place a spear under the armpit, if you need one; then take a very long bandage of a palm in width, then lay double cloth over bandages, and plaster; then take a thin splint of three inches in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage so that the end of the bandage is hanging; and place the splint on the break, and turn the bandage over the shoulder joint, and under the healthy armpit, and under the sick armpit; and loosen it from each part, and when you see that the binding holds the break well, and you clearly see that the splint is not moving over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the bindings grow loose, then tighten them; and make the patient sit on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit, so that the aid can be lifted up high; this will ease the break of the shoulder by the alignment of the arm, or you bind the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad events come, until twenty days; then start the plaster again, if you see that there is need for it, and tighten and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in twenty-eight days, and less in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	The shoulder breaks or becomes too loose and cannot hold its place, and one must know how to treat it through touch; if the shape of the break appears according to its figure, and you reset it according to its natural form in all ways that you can; then put on the place flour from the mill with abundance of egg, and light cloths, and double the cloth on top; then put a large and subtle bandage on, one pace larger than the shoulder, and under the bandage there are hooks in any place of the shoulder, so that the hair of linen ties bind it equally; and then tie it all with a strong band tightly, so that the band does not move from its place, and inspect the bond every day; and each time when it loosens, tie it again, and put the bandage back on if it has moved from its place, and lay the patient on their side. The shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five, And when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure, for it is not bone that will come loose easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone sticks out and points under the skin, then take it up and draw it out, and do what we have said to calm an abscess or hot swelling.
de la brisure dou pis	Il semble que vous avez mentionné un autre type de blessure, celle du "pis" (probablement le poitrail ou le bassin).
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bones are sometimes broken inside, but this is rare; but they often break at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken inside, it slants downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks nourishment, and becomes thin, and by chance may vomit blood, and opens up the sinews in the broken bone, and they feel sick.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on their back, and they place .i. (one) cushion between their shoulders, then press the shoulders, and join the ribs of .ij. (two) ribs with their hands, and carefully try to put it together in every way you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply ointments and bandages on top of the staff made of salt or other light wood, and wrap it around the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the strap back behind, and tighten it slightly, and release each hour a little, and if it swells, then tighten it; and if it seems convenient to unfasten, due to corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and clean the ointment, and address what has come from ways of cures; then rinse the ointment, and tie it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	C'est l'objet du texte que nous avions ! Le titre semble être une référence à un manuscrit médiéval qui traite de la fracture des côtes.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not come but in the thick places after the back, and to the head inside, and do not bend but because they are slippery; and one senses well at the examination of the shoulders.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedy is that you set it straight again as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a poultice and bind with an iron band, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is sloping inward, then the patient feels very great pain and pricking, as well as a feeling like pleurisy, because the bone punctures the membrane; and he laments with sharp pains, and chokes and vomits a great quantity of blood, and this is a serious condition, and in the past they have used great remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that it is necessary to administer foods which inflate the belly, so as to push the breakage outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot abscesses form there, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has already come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And among us, one said that you should put cups on the place to suck out strongly, and it seems like a good reason; however, there is doubt that the cups may attract the superfluities to the place because of its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And among us, one said that you should cover the place with wet wool soaked in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to put the linen back in its place, then treat it as if it were a case of pleurisy, meat wound, and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure because of the bone which presses against the skin, and doubt is in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken ribcage, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to ward off infection; and then one must cut into the bone and draw out lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat them with poultices until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess forms, place on dampened cloths in rose oil and apply to the affected area; and cure the wound as it is necessary for the abscess, and be careful over the surrounding skin where it should be until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a breakage comes to the bones of the neck, and it breaks, causing the person to bend down; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, look closely and see if their hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move or stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when one holds them and pricks them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient has been cured, if a cure is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, look closely and see if the feet are softened, and if there is stiffness in the hands that comes from it, and on the back there is windy swelling and vomiting without will; and when one has been made comfortable in their belly, there is vomiting without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he lies on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly: the patient must not labor at all in their treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you put something on it if there is an hot abscess, if you put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is calmed down; then put a comforting and drying poultice on it and tie it with a cloth, and command the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel pain, until they are cured.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone breaks loose, it is necessary to cover the wound with a cloth; and remove the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if they are large, with a suture, then heal the wound with ointment dripping with fat, until it is cured. And if the splinter of the bone is broken, which is called "the splinter of the cow", put your fist from your left hand into it and place it equal to the other hand in your power, then put the poultice and bandage on it, if you need them; then tighten it, and if there are loose bones, make a splint on it, remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Here's a rough translation:
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	A small diminishment occurs in the head when the bones of the back are broken; and if it happens, then there is not much reduction in height; and they become two long ones, and decline towards each other, and come to the patient with pain at the place, and a puncture, and inflammation where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above it, as much as the breakage; and know what the breakage is and its shape; and if the breakage is only in the head alone, then put this same breakage back in its natural place.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is long, or it declines inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach, as much as the restoration of this breakage will become apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it back in place, then apply the splint, and then apply a wedge of wood or of horn, and bind the breakage so that it does not move; and fill the space under the ribs, as much as the swelling is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess forms there, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed down, and apply what we have said before that; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as it should be, if no bad accident occurs; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	La brisure de l'ajutoire (ou de la cuisse)
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The assistants are those who are between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two manners: one of which is that you take one straight branch from a green twig, larger in size.
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the branch together with two pieces of string, and let it hang down, and have the patient sit on one seat; then throw the broken arm above the branch so that it comes into place, and has a wooden curve in the middle; then make the patient hang from any heavy thing or the servants stretch it downwards; then place the physician's hands equally on the fracture, until the break returns to its proper place.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one straps the patient on their bed, and ties their hand to their neck, then commands two servants to have one pull what is above the fracture to his hands, and the other to pull from below all the strings, and stretch each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then hold tightly to the strip below the cut and above it, and stretch each of the attendants to their share.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the cut is near the head of the shoulder, you must put the middle strip under the shoulder and the other towards the neck, under the cut; and also if the cut is towards the neck, it is necessary to put the lighter strip, without labor, until the cut is even on the place and on the neck; then put equal the cutting, as is necessary, and hold it, so that swelling does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come, then don't strain it at all for seven days, and put a warm compress on linen oil on the arm and shoulder, until the abscess is calmed down; then strain it, and the way to strain it is that you put the splint above the fracture, then assemble the arm with a support, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the cloth, and strain above the support, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, if no other thing prevents it, or if the bone has not been moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone has not been moved, use splints, and place above the fracture a larger and stronger splint than the others, with two inches between each one, and have each splint be so large that it passes over the break three inches from each side; then strain on the splints, in such a way as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, stronger and less distanced.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the sitting of the stars and the straining, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot swelling, then leave it alone for seven days, as we have said; then look at each day three times, so that itching or inflammation does not come to the place, or the discoloration cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the head of the arm, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, do not loosen it until after three days or more, and the patient lies on their back with hands on their stomach; and places under the shoulder one pillow full of wool evenly, and observes each hour of day or night that the fracture of the broken limb does not move, or that the ligaments become loose; if the arm is set by the virtue of medicine, and gives it food as we have mentioned before, in such a manner that the food be at the first subtleties; and when he begins to regain strength, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is custom that the shoulder and leg should be reset within forty days from then; and then one must loosen and administer bath and ointments for medicine to set it in place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and stuck, then it stays to be untied for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one small and one large, with the small one at the shoulder and the large one below it; by chance, you may break either the small or the large bone alone, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restorations are light, and the healings; and when the large ones are broken, then the healing is bad, and more painful than when they were broken together at once.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken only, then you must make a splint slightly extended and straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone, then you must tie it more tightly; and stretch it on the cushion, and raise the splint of the hand higher than the others, and the little ones lower than the others, and that the patient cross his arms over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any further pain; then extend the servant's arm to the part below his hand, or to the elbow, and another servant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the glass equally, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces, then put each one back in its place, and if any is dislocated that you can't restore it to its place, then send for a surgeon, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is a wound, I've spoken about it in the chapter on singular wounds; then take care of the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration a hot abscess arises, then apply an ointment made from rose oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the cloth on top gently, until the hot abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the ointment, and put the plaster made from mill dust with a great deal of egg white on it; next place the stars, and let the star for the breaking be a little stronger, and somewhat larger than the others; and know that there should be six stars or branches in more or less disposition: whether the break is in one bone, or two; and hold the break up higher than any other part, and always less far away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths which are over the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the strings by which it is strained be made of linen, nor too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident comes to the member, such as itching which comes to the member, then it is necessary that you apply hot water to the member until those itchings are calmed down; and let the member rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then reapply the stretching, and if the joint is loosened and the bone has become separated, and similar thing, then correct it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too narrow, then you should moisten it with one pess (i.e., a poultice) and let it be for some days until the swelling flows into it, and then tie.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not loosen him until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or in addition, have him lay his hands on his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this break is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the mixtures and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and in its arm there occur many kinds of breaks, and it comes to be creased or bent many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the wrist of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient cross their legs and sit straight in front of them equally; then put their hand on the stretched sheet, and stretch out the splints over the broken bones, and place them even with the mirror, so long as they are well joined together; and apply the plaster and bandages, if swelling comes, then put an iron band according to the size of the wrist; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is around the side of the wrist near the stomach, make a ball of cloth, and command the patient to squeeze it against their broken wrist; and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the iron band be as soft as possible, but also large enough for the wrist, and bind it in the same way.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, it is necessary that you put an iron band on top and another underneath in the wrist, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the bones.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of the bones of the wrist, and it is the thumb, then put them equal, as is necessary; and bind with the wrist, and if you see that you should put a small straight iron band to lift the break, and do not move it; and if the break is in another bone, such as the index or one of the others, then put them equal, and tie with the healthy bone that is behind; or tie them all together in one holding, which is worth something, or put a splint on top, as you would for a thumb; and take care of the restoration and the disposition of the swelling that comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Il semble que nous ayons terminé la lecture de ce texte médical ancien. Voulez-vous continuer avec une autre partie du texte ? Ou bien est-ce pour une raison spécifique que vous avez mentionné "de la cuixe brisie" ?
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	Il semble que nous ayons repris le texte médical ancien.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then stretches each limb to its equal part; and this is when the breakage is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near to the root of the thigh, then it will be one of the tendons that goes towards the elbow, and the other tendons below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near to the knee, and then it will be one of the tendons near the knee, and the other below; then place the mirrors so that the bone is equal in both hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then put the splint and the bandage, so that the abscesses do not come back.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, so let it subside then return to your work and care for the patient; the bandaging is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap a strong doubled bandage over the break on the leg in three or four layers, and leave the superfluous parts; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the buttock, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg below, and have the end of the thread come up; then turn back down on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then put stitches on the break on the leg, and put a stitch on the bone of the leg; then place the eight threads between the leg and the thigh made of soft cloth to keep it even; then start to tie firmly three or four turns above the break; and when you get higher up from the break, loosen the strain; then take the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, and bind three stitches that are on top, then go back down to the end of the thread until you reach the foot; and if it does not move from its place, then leave it so, and if there is no abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it swells, so let it be untied and address what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, so it is necessary to remove them if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut the area, and extract whatever can be extracted; and then cure as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never once is the thigh broken in such a way that one puts splints on it, as on the arm or leg; nevertheless, in this kind of treatment the patient does not suffer.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one day, or a little more or less, according to the various constitutions of the patients.
de la ruelle dou genoil	De la rupture du genou.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that there is often a small break in the joint of the knee, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only by a crack or an incision, and there is great pain, and not little pain, and this seems quite severe.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is thus: you put back what was broken to its place, so that it can move again as much as possible; then apply an ointment, and if necessary, insert a rounded wooden splint, and bind it as needed, then re-align all the dislocations which we have mentioned in other fractures, such as warm compresses and similar treatments. Then apply to each accident what is fitting for it, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of a break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, from which one is called "humerus", and the other is called "fibula"; and it has all the same break as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone (fibula) is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the big bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen well; and it turns beneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply an extension, and place it equally, and tie the bandages equally; but nevertheless, it is necessary if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, that the extension be minor and more lightweight; and loosen according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your operation, take two wooden splints that cover the leg from one end to the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap them in two layers of bandages, one on top and one on the bottom, and bind them together in the middle, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus it is well. And some administer a wooden bar of the length of the leg, and made of wood, and put the leg in it to prevent movement, and properly clean the wound in the break; and move each day the leg, to see if there is warm swelling or another accident; and treat it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of a break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle rarely breaks, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and crush, and there is no other injury than bruising in many cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot break and you see these bones overlapping each other, then place the sick foot on the earth, just like it would go, and then put your own foot on top of it, where the bones are raised, and press down so that they return to their proper place; then apply the splint and bandage above, and under the foot of the hurt foot a small board with two grooves, then tie it firmly to the foot with string or thread, then wrap cloth around, and other things which you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find that the bones are equalized, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, restore them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put a splint on the broken toe, according to the length of the toe, and make it a little wider, then place under the foot that board which I mentioned, and tie it firmly in place; and if there are two or three or more toes broken, then put a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and tie the board under the foot securely; and have the end of the board projecting out from the foot, so that it is well fastened.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other breaks, as we have discussed; and treat each accident according to what is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of a break of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's hip is broken, so let her sit and be enlarged, then incline her towards the back part of the spine, and have it held from behind; then fill the natural opening of the patient with cotton, and insert as much as you can into it; then lift up the woman, and raise the back a little bit by little, and thus let the cotton jump, until it reaches the entrance of the natural opening, and comes back the bone with the flesh; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in place, and do this for seven days or so: then the break will be restored, and if you want, take a bladder from a goat, and attach a string to the anus, and insert the whole bladder into the natural opening; then blow into the string strongly, until the bladder is inflated inside: the natural opening will come back the bone; then fill it with cotton, and leave it thus for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the elbow of the man is broken, or of the woman, so restore it thus as we have said in the bone of the hip; and these recent breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and practice into it and pays attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For a break signifies in many positions the right way of restoration: listen then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloth around it and leave it for three days or so: and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or arm or similar, that he be healed immediately, so that the stitches which we have said may witness to.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals and an abscess forms, then close it with pitch, or if you have nothing else, then start to restore the break in that very same hour or day, so that pus does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus comes out, then let the restoration alone for just nine days, until the abscess is calmed down, and do not touch it on the tenth day or the quarter, because you would bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the skin's surface, it is necessary that you gently point it out with your fingers, making a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for you to put on level with your hands, then take this instrument made of iron, which has 7 or 8 prongs of length, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the doctor that he takes 3 or 4, as needed in each cure of break; and it should be rounded and a little thick, so that it does not bend when compressed on the member under your work, and it should be sharp at the end, and thick at the middle in front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason the curved head should be placed on the top of the visible bone; and press it once, until it returns, and so that they are equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, it is necessary that you cut off the top of the bone, so that the instrument may have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot put the bone back in place as we have said, then cut it off with an instrument suitable for this, or a saw or knife, to your power; and take out from the bone what is remaining of sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reduced and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
