Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So that it remains in its place, then wet the cloth in black wine of a styptic and put it on properly; and do not put cerote or any oil upon the wound, lest it bring forth corruption and rot; then administer stitches when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not bound with the breakage; and many times this has been done by foolish healers, and they have brought upon the patient death or corruption on occasion; and it is a more gentle and softer constriction than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad event will come from it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then do not put on stitches; but envelop all around, instead of stitches, with hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the bow is inflamed towards the wound, so remove what you have put on top of it in vinegar and put on a healing salve for wounds, such as tetrofarcation salve and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the member twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and cured.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be bound in such a way that the lower part bends slightly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot heal but instead turns into a swelling, know that it has small bones, so you should sew the wound with thread, and remove all these loose pieces of bone that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess or some other manner of corruption comes to the place, so it behooves you that you treat it, according to what is said in its chapter before this.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and protrudes on the limb, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder, and other similar things in the great limbs, do not remove it, for many times it comes to death, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, so leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	the blisters that come on the scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come across this after the healing of the break, especially when it's near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the figure of the member; and perhaps it cannot make its natural movements.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care if the blister is fresh: if the administrator uses purgative medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, aloe, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with purgative wine or with almond oil or with vinegar; and put them on the new blister in poultices, and apply pressure well, and do not remove it for one day; and then release it, and start another, as long as the nodules are removed; or you strain against a well-made piece of cloth, because the properties of the cloth are such that they remove all swellings on the members; and if the nodule has already become hardened like a stone, and it is necessary to remove it, so scrape off the superfluous parts above, or take it to a barber, as long as it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	from the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone break is restored, and the limb remains weak and fragile, it happens for many reasons: one of them is that it was tied too tightly, and not tightened as needed; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment to the member could not come; or due to a multitude of swellings; or because of excessive movements, not in its right time; or because it has too little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make food for the sick person, and make their body tender, until there is a multiplication of blood in them; and administer baths to them, and give them joy and comfort; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and removes excess fluid, as often as water can, until the nourishment comes to the member; and returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	from the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the member is ugly, though it doesn't lose its natural function: don't believe the fools who say that you should break the whole limb again, and many foolish healers have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and leads to great harm, and possibly death. However, if the nodules and the twisting are fresh, it is necessary to remove them with hot water or mild herbs, such as leaves of marjoram, roots, and melilotus, and similar things; and make a mollifying plaster, such as well-made dyaquilon, and take the milky sap of marjoram, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or take plump figs, and grind them with henbane seeds, and similar medicines that soften the inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And at times is taken out the pustule by constant and long rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be a movement to the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, so that it must cover just up to the bone, slightly lightly with a sharp incisor; and apply cauterization and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of Dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is caused by a joint moving out of its place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs to anyone, if now it needs to be returned to its original position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one waits, the swelling will grow, and perhaps when one returns it causes pain at the place; therefore it is not necessary to move it until it has grown swollen: many times brings spasms and other pains; nonetheless, when this happens, so heal the patient first, then leave him, until the abscess has been alleviated; then warm the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each member as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head up to the foot.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Whatever happens when the jawbones are dislocated inwards, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: or they are a little pulled out of their place, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor close its mouth, and encircle its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it heals in a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you should reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in this manner that the attendants may hold the patient's head, and place the mirror's cap on the end of one of their hands into the root of the jaw dislocation within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands are outside to make it equal; and instruct the patient to relax his mandibles, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the servants place the cloth equally on both sides, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it's difficult to return, even if it's the two jawbones together, then heat them with hot water and oil, until they are rinsed lightly; nor delay in returning, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back into balance, and the patient's mouth is tightly closed with a soothing ointment, then place damp cloths on the cheeks made from rose oil and wax, then tie them lightly with soft strings; and the patient lies on their back, and his jaws should be between two pillows, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor does he exert himself to masticate, but takes light food until the pains are removed, and the jawbones are numbed; and then eat whatever they want lightly, and do not work at opening their mouth to eat and drink, as long as the jawbone is well numbed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not turned back to their positions, then fever and sharp stomachaches come, and perhaps intestinal purging, and perhaps vomiting of clean bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a death sentence; and many times the person who has this dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the elbow
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The elbow cannot be straightened from the inside towards the shoulder, and it is dislocated only once to the outside, and then one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back often and extends their arms; then press firmly with your palm to its place, and it will return; then put on the poultice and bandage and restrain it; and the shoulder that is near the ribcage cannot dislocate again; if not, and if it dislocates once, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on the poultice and bandage, and restrain it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus the shoulder of the scapula is returned to its place when it is out of joint.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: it dislocates to the part of the armpit below; and it dislocates to the part of the bone; and by chance it dislocates upwards, and this happens often; and it does not dislocate back for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, indeed in those who have a lot of fat, because they fall easily down; to those who have enough fat, they stumble down slowly, and recover slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that there is a blow or a crushing, and the shoulder swells with a hot tumor, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you should examine it thoroughly until you are certain; and once you have confirmed the diagnosis, begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it falls towards the armpit, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them a manifest diversity; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and below the armpit to the toucher's hand the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its place, nor move with any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly at the toucher's hand; and this way of dislocation is not to be reset, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the physician lifts the hand of the patient up high, then puts his thumbs under the blade, and lifts the joint with force upwards to its place; and the physician lifts the hand and stretches it up, then places it down; and it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in three days after, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and a poultice applied freshly soothing and relieving, such as decoction of althea and fenugreek and meilote in water, and should be applied; then the patient should be placed on their back, and under the shoulder an equal woolen pad is put, not too soft or too hard, then the heel of the doctor puts a mirror on it, and lifts the head of the shoulder strongly, and pulls the hand of the patient; and another minister will hold the head of the patient so that it does not move down; that shoulder comes back immediately, and if you see it to reduce in this manner: and it is that you should make a man who is greater than the patient present; and be straight towards the opposite side, and thrust his shoulder under the arm of the patient, and lift the arm up so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister will pull the hand of the patient down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can carry something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And you also straighten him in another way: and it is to stick a long burning iron into the earth, whose head is as rounded as a pestle, and not too big or too thin; then it is put under the patient, but so that it sticks softly on them, and the patient's hand should be as long as the length of the shaft; then his hand should extend downwards from the other side in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	...then tie the wooden rod wrapped around with a cloth in such a way that it does not pierce the patient, then place the wood under the blade of the patient; and extend your arm on top of the wooden rod, and tie the assistant's arm to the rod at the hand, then put the arm over a beam about four fists wide, and extend the hands downwards, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will be restored now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	...And when it is restored, however it may be, it is necessary that you place under the blade a linen rod of equal thickness, then apply the plastering mixture with powder from the mill, with incense and egg white, on all the shoulder and around it; then gently strap the bandage under the blade, and turn the strap over the plaster, and hold the hand to the neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	...And it is necessary that you dress the wound with poultice, as long as the members are comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then re-dress more later, in 5 or 7 days, and move it around; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come in, or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply cauters to three pores, as it is shown in the chapter on cauters.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	...And if you do all of this and the joint does not stay together after 7 days, and it cannot lift your arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut, stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place. (Note: This suggests a serious and irreversible injury to the nerve)
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	...The dislocation that occurs in the chest, shoulders, or back is caused by forceful throwing or stretching of the arms, and requires another treatment method; and it should be treated until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes stiffness to the member, and slow movement, so the patient bathes many times, until that stiffness is alleviated, and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	from a dislocation hurt
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint from a hurt is swollen to a point, and returns to its point; and it's swollen all around, as well in front and behind, and the dislocation isn't reset, because you can see it well and feel it well; and swells according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick person's cut with the blood, so you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the dislocation is high up, and cannot bend the arm, nor reach the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it's necessary that you clean it while the suppurating swellings come, because if the suppurating swellings come, it would be grievous to reduce it; and perhaps can't be reduced completely at all, especially when it is in the back; so it's worse than other dislocations, and is of more great pain, and perhaps death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the reduction is such, when it can be reduced, that you stretch out its hand with both of your hands; and its arm is spread out, and the hands of the person according to the joint around, above and below, and push the joint into its pockets together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when it doubles its hand to its own hand, and presses the joint which is swollen at the root of the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and that two ministers stretch the arm, and bind it with two bandages, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm from each side, then wrap a double long and wide cloth around it; and when the skilled person has joined the joint to their hand, they will anoint the joint with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is back in place, they put on dry plaster with egg yolks, and bind it firmly, and let the arm hang at the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, then unbind it and let it be; and if you see that the joint doesn't hold well, start again with the plaster and the bandage, and leave it for a few days, until it's tightly fixed; then unbind it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset and it moves, then bathe him and rub him well, and press on it until it is relieved; or you put a sheep's fat compress on the joint, then let it stay for a day and a night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the compress back on, and then have him enter the bath; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see fit, put a moistened and heated pad of marshmallow root on it, and press on it; then it will return to its proper place.

Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand becomes swollen and the reduction is light, almost like other joints. However, it's necessary to reduce it quickly, even when it's still swollen, or if there's an abscess that has formed with hot pus.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is that you put the patient's hand on a table, and extend their limb, and have the examiner place it level, so that they put their palm over the appearance of the joint, and then push down until it returns; however, it is necessary for you to look if it is well in place; then have the patient put the back of their hand on a table at extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is on the back of the hand, instruct the patient to place their back of their hand over a table, and the surgeon puts his hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it now returns (into place), that is well If not, then have the patient apply poultices soothing the abscesses, and let them be without reapplying.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you can't put it back in place after any days, then the joint remains twisted; and do not apply anything to the patient that is hot until the hand is softened, and he can no longer strain anything: then know that the nerves are cut or the arteries are severed; unless there is another cause more severe than straining by a fire cautery near the case, and perhaps it's worth nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is back in place, then put on the poultice that we've said, and strain it and let it be for five days, then unbind it and let it go like that again.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he can't move his hand well and there's still some pain, then soak it in hot water and rub it gently until he's cured.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	It seems we're discussing another type of joint injury. Let me know if you'd like to continue reading or ask questions about the text!
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	At times the thumb of the hand is dislocated to each side, at times to the back of the palm or the belly; then the thumb becomes bent and you push the dislocation into your pouches as much as it returns, then hold the head of the thumb and lead it towards the part where it was separated; and leave it for two days, and then put it in place on that day; and from now on bind it, as we have said, and loosen it every day, and move it and rebind it at night; and do this often, until it is tight, and do just the same if it is dislocated to the belly of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healed; and do also, when it is dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	It seems we're discussing a different type of injury now: the swelling of the spine in the back. Let me know if you'd like to continue reading or ask questions about this section!
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine in the back or neck is swollen, or there are multiple swellings, it's not possible to treat them because the disease is spreading quickly and hastening the patient's condition.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the evacuations shoot forth without voluntary intention, nor can they hold it, and many times are softened some member, or both thighs or both arms, or sometimes the spine moves to four parts; that which moves towards the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you return if the gilbositez comes from infancy: if there is no cure nor healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or percussion or similar things, the old manner of cures by great words say there is little in all great profit; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositeit that comes to the chest before, there is no cause nor health; and also the one that comes straightly to both sides, and one cannot cure those that come improperly to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient lies on his face in a straight place, and has strain underneath him, so he does not hurt himself; then insert two tongs at the head into the earth firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a strap behind the joints of the patient, and another around the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two attendants know the straps, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two tongs; and are well fastened, the tongs as we have said, and the physician places his palms on the spine firmly, so it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a board three arms long, and hollow out the back side, and have the patient lie on their side, and place the head of the board under the plexus; then put the middle of the board over the spine; and have the patient put their feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see that it will not return, do this in the turning which turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then take two skewers as long as the patient's arm, and have two others towards their feet, and have between each skewer, in the middle and under, a space of a span wide; and have on each skewer one turn, or where the tendon is curved, and let the skewers be firmly in the earth so they do not move; and between each two skewers have one turning stick, for to turn the tendon; and then tie the string that is among the tendons towards the head, and the other string towards the feet to the other turning stick, and have both assistants turn their sticks to all of the string, and the master straighten the spine as we said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is evened out, place desiccative ointment with plenty of egg on top, and then cover it up, and then bind with a strip of wood three fingers long, so that it may reattach the place of the joint and the healthy part of the spine; then bind it with a string, as we have said, and use gentle poultices on the patient until they are healed; and if any obstacle comes at the end of the healing, you must administer softening medicines and soothers with the strip that we have mentioned before; and one time administer a piece of fat, and another time it becomes evident in the back part of the spine near the backbone, and think it is dislocation; and it is the bone that splits open, so one should not have any presumption: perchance would bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	It seems we're discussing another type of injury now: the dislocation of the thigh (hainche). Let me know if you'd like to continue reading or ask questions about this section!
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It's known that the joints of the thigh and the shoulder come apart only through dislocation, and not in the same way as other joints. The joint of the thigh is swollen in four parts: inside and outside, and in front and back; and more severely inside than outside, and swelling in front and back. It seems like a description of the specific symptoms and characteristics of a hip dislocation.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is this: when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee swells more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee at all; and there is a place nearby that becomes inflamed with an abscess, because the head of the thigh bone comes to that place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which comes from the outside is that this accident is contrary to those in front. It seems like a description of a type of hip dislocation where the affected limb is positioned opposite to its normal position, possibly with the femur head pointing outwards rather than inwards.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that which happens in front are that the leg is bent well according to its completion; however, it cannot bend its knee joint without pain, and if you want to make it walk, it can't move forward, and holds its urine, and swells up the groin, and when it walks, it passes over the heel. It seems like a description of symptoms associated with a hip dislocation where the affected limb is positioned in an abnormal way, causing pain and difficulty walking or moving the knee joint.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that which happens behind are that it cannot extend its knee joint, nor bend it, and the affected leg is more bent than the other, and the groin is softened, and the veins of the thigh are at the same level as the sides. It seems like a description of symptoms associated with a hip dislocation where the affected limb is positioned in an abnormal way, causing stiffness and softening of the groin area.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation are that you treat it if the dislocation is ancient and has remained in its position, without any cure; and do not have any presumption about it. It seems like a warning to be cautious when treating hip dislocations, especially those that have been present for a long time, as they may be more difficult or impossible to cure.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that where the dislocation is fresh and it's of three types of dislocation, hasten to turn the joint back into place, and make it straight inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and there will be no need for any other treatment. It seems like a description of an emergency procedure to correct a fresh hip dislocation by manually manipulating the joint back into its proper position, with the hope that it will heal on its own without further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you should have strong assistants, and steady the leg strongly with both hands, or tie it to one ligature above the knee; and another assistant should stretch his hand down in such a way that he pushes his hands under his buttocks, then hold him with a soft ligature on the thigh; and another should grasp the chief part of the ligature; and all stretch upwards and downwards at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at one time, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for all three types of dislocations, and if the dislocation has returned to its proper place, as we have said, then it's good. It seems like a confirmation that this technique can be used effectively for different types of hip dislocations, and that a successful outcome is desirable.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then it is necessary to apply a cure to its resemblance. When the dislocation is at the part that has been stretched, then you should support the patient on his healthy side, then put the ligature on the root of the thigh, and the place which is under the angle, then stretch the ligature upwards towards the angle, and towards the furthest point; then take another assistant's arms, and encircle the large part of the sick person's thigh, and extend it far out: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you cannot compress it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the patient's two feet together with a strong soft cord on both heels and ankles; and let the affected leg be extended two fingers more than the other ones; then let it be hung from the top of a beam, and above the ground hold up one long arm; then command the servant to grasp the patient's hips, and let another servant hang along with the patient, who grasp the hips firmly, because the joint comes back quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is far gone, have the patient lie down, as we said in the case of sciatica, and stretch the cord over the affected leg properly, and on the hip also; then put two torches, one at the head and the other at the feet, then stick the torch between the hips on the patient in the form; and wet cloths are placed around so that he does not hurt the patient, then each servant stretches out towards him, and the doctor puts something equal to his hand on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put them on the table and press them thus as we have said in the Galenism, and place the patient on the right side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it's necessary to stretch the sick leg hastily and according to what I've said; and have the person who knows how to do it put their hand on top of the patient's affected groin area, then press with the other hand, and extend downwards towards the knee. It seems like a description of a technique where pressure is applied to try to reduce the dislocation, possibly by using both hands to manipulate the affected limb in a specific way.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is on the outside, it should not extend the patient downward, nor lift them up from the earth, but rather that they should be as if the hip were dislocated outward, as we have said about lying on two hips; and should be on their back, and the ligatures should be stretched as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table; and it will be fine when the patient stretches out their legs, and they will be even; then place the clavicles together, and apply the plaster, and strain with a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three days or four, then loosen it, and put the plaster on; and if you see that they are even, strain again as before, and let them rest for three days; then loosen it, and make them go slowly, until the member is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The kneecap is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend their leg at their knee, and if it does not bend at its knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet; then take hold of their knee with your hands, and pull between your arms, then bend both sides of the knee firmly; and another assistant extends their foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it bends well at its knee lightly; and apply the plaster on top, and make the leg rest in the knee, and bind them together tightly for three days or four, then release; and do not let the patient move, until the member is comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not in place, administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes sprained and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tend towards the part where it has been dislocated: the return is easy, and one must stretch it lightly with their hands when it is only felt.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, you must make the patient sit up straight, and have the assistants hold him firm through the leg, above the ankle; then take the foot to yourself with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and push the foot upwards well; and do this two times, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start again the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix the passel firmly in the earth between his thighs, and tie a cloth around him so he does not harm the patient; then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another stretch the foot with their hands or with a strap that they tie above the ankle of the foot; then each assistant stretches equally, and the passel will be thus between the thighs of the patient to keep the patient when you are stretching him; then put the misaligned place into the hands of one of the assistants, and have another assistant pinch the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, then put the poultice and bandages on top, and bind it tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and take care that the bandage is not too tight; then let it be for two days or three, and if the bandage becomes loose, rebind it; then release it on the fourth day, and have the patient rest for four days; and if he walks before this time, it is not sure that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms on the heel, it is advisable that you treat it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is sound.
des dois	of the toes
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the toes are dislocated, they should be gently stretched without force, and it is a slight thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any of the joints of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you have the patient sit on a smooth surface or on a straight table, and place your foot over this joint, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; and when it is even and there is nothing apparent, place under the heel of the foot a board two fingers thick, then bind it tightly, and let it be for three days, then release it; and have him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and one wants to restore it, many times the patient will die: do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor bold; and use at first soothing remedies on hot abscesses, and leave the patient to God's hand if you do not see hope of recovery; and when you see hope, then reset the member to its place, so that the hot abscess will come; and when the member is in place, administer soothing remedies for the hot abscess, and treat the wound as it needs, with drying ointments; and if with dislocation there is breakage and small bones splintered, remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, because this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge that will arm and fortify your body.
Amen	So be it (a phrase of affirmation)
